Important Domestic News Two

Luo Lin's Division Recovers Shanggao 79

Bandit Suppression Divisions United as One

Hu Zuyu's Troops Have Arrived in Jiujiang

According to a Nanchang communication from the 9th Route Army Headquarters, the main force of the Communist bandits Zhu and Mao is currently along the Gan River in Jianxia, Ji'an. The Peng and Huang factions are along the Yuan River in Fenyi and Xinyu. The 18th Division of the bandit suppression troops is still on the line of Zhangshu, Xingan, and Qingjiang. The New 5th Division is in Gaoan, and the New 13th Division is in Fuzhou. There has been no major change. The general attack order is expected to be issued in early next month. However, recently, the Zhu, Peng, and Huang factions attacked and captured Shanggao from Xinyu and Jianxia, attempting to cut off the connection between Yuanzhou's Luo Lin and Gaoan's Gong Bingfan. Fortunately, Luo, the commander of the 77th Division, ordered Tao's brigade to garrison Yuanzhou. Yi and Xi's two brigades launched a fierce attack on the bandits in Shanggao from Yuanzhou, and on the 27th, they recovered Shanggao, killing countless bandits. The 9th Route Army Headquarters received a report from Commander Luo detailing the situation, which stated that early this morning, Yi and Xi's two brigades, led by Yuan, searched and suppressed the bandits along the way through Licun and Yangqiao. The troops advanced to Hantang. Gan Yin ordered Yi's brigade to break through the bandits in Meiyuegang through Xiongtang and personally led Xi's brigade through Jiangkou to recover Shanggao at noon. Many bandits were killed successively. According to prisoners, the bandits used the 3rd, 4th, 12th, and 20th armies to attack Shanggao from Xiajiang through Xinyu, attempting to cut off the connection between Luo and Gong's divisions. Fortunately, they were all defeated by us. After Luo's victory in Shanggao, a part of the Communist bandits advanced from Qingjiang Shanggao to Gaoan. The Chen Guangyao and Luo Shouyi brigades of the 50th Division immediately set off from Shengmi and Wanshou Palace in Ganjiang and advanced towards Gaoan. The Gong Bingfan division in Gaoan then moved upwards to Shanggao to connect with Luo's division. Therefore, a line has been formed from Pingxiang through Yuanzhou, Shanggao, and Gaoan to Nanchang.

The Jiujiang and Nanchang-Xunyang Road in northern Jiangxi are extremely important. After Liu Yi's brigade opened Fengxin and Jing'an, the 20th Division of Xu Kexiang was stationed there. Xu originally planned to open the Raozhou-Jingdezhen area in eastern Jiangxi after the 5th Division arrived in Jiujiang. Currently, the 28th and 29th regiments of the 5th Division of Hu Zuyu have arrived in Jiujiang. Hu took a special train on the Nanchang-Xunyang Road to the province on the 28th to ask Commander Lu for instructions and plans to stay for a day or two before returning to Xunyang to defend. In order to consolidate the rear and mobilize the people to participate in the eradication of the Communists, the municipal government, the provincial capital public security bureau organized watch teams, while the city party headquarters organized anti-communist groups and propaganda teams to promote publicity.

(October 28)

Cai Tingkai, Commander of the Sixtieth Division, Returns to Guangdong 80

Requesting Resignation or Possible Reduction of His Troops

To Meet with Commander Chen in Wu and Then Enter Hospital for Treatment

Guangzhou Correspondence: Cai Tingkai, Commander of the Sixtieth Division, recently led his troops back south after participating in the battles along the Longhai and Pinghan lines. His troops are temporarily stationed in Hanzhong. Commander Cai himself, due to stomach illness, returned to Guangdong alone for treatment. On the 24th, he arrived in Hong Kong on the President Coolidge from Shanghai. After staying in Hong Kong for one night, he took a Foshan ship back to Guangdong on the 25th. The ship arrived in the province at 2:15 PM. Prior to this, various heads of agencies flocked to the pier to welcome him. Commander Cai shook hands with each person as a greeting, and then took a car to the Eighth Route Army Headquarters to rest. He returned to his private residence at 4:00 PM in the afternoon. The press rushed to interview him. According to Cai's remarks, roughly speaking, a month ago, he led the Sixtieth Division to Hanzhong. At that time, it was planned that the Sixtieth Division would be responsible for the Jinpu Line, and the Sixty-first Division would be responsible for the Longhai Line. Later, the plan changed and they jointly attacked Tai'an, and then captured Jinan. After the remnants of Yan's troops crossed the river and retreated, the Sixtieth and Sixty-first Divisions were ordered to transfer to the Pinghan and Longhai lines, successively attacking Xinzheng, Zhengzhou, Kaifeng, and Lanfeng, with irresistible force. Feng's troops were defeated and fled in disarray. The Central Army thus achieved a triumphant return. Feng and Yan's losses in this defeat were no less than 150,000 men. The losses of our army were comparable to those during the campaign against Gui, but with repeated replenishments, our strength remained intact. Now, the troops are gathered in Hanzhong. Once the Central Government's orders are received, they will go south to suppress bandits, but the destination will be determined at that time and cannot be announced in advance. The Eighth Route Army is now fully capable of dealing with the remnants of the Gui province forces. If necessary, the Nineteenth Route Army can also join in. As for the resignation issue, I am quite determined. Previously, when this division was under the Eleventh Army, it received orders to reduce its size, and the Tenth Division was reduced to a brigade. Then, due to the military emergency, it was expanded back into a division. I will only follow the Central Government's orders. Now that the national military has been pacified, I am specially returning military power to the Central Government and awaiting its disposition. If the Central Government does not approve my resignation, I request that my troops be reduced in size to save military expenses and engage in construction. In the near future, I plan to take leave for rest and recuperation. Once I have time, I will go to Wu to meet with Commander Chen Jitang to report on the Northern Expedition, and then return to the province to enter the hospital for treatment, making sure to eliminate the root of the illness to avoid recurrence of stomach problems. (Evening of October 25)

Japanese Foreign Deputy Minister Nagai Arrives in Jinan 81

The Jinan Telephone Company's Japanese Debt Case 82

Jinan Correspondence: The Jinan Telephone Company was established in the fourth year of the Republic. General Manager Ma Guanhe (i.e., Ma Huijie) was in charge for ten years and incurred a debt of 1.2 million yuan. When the company was reorganized in the 14th year of the Republic, the board of directors decided to dismiss Ma Guanhe and issue 1.2 million yuan in bonds to repay the debt. In the past six years, 400,000 yuan had been repaid successively. Unexpectedly, recently, Kagawa Shoichi, the general manager of the Japanese-owned Toyo Takushoku Kabushiki Kaisha, entrusted Yoshida Kan, a Japanese, as his representative, and also engaged Mou Shaozhou, a lawyer from Qingdao, as the Japanese representative's deputy. They filed a lawsuit in the Jinan District Court, claiming that Ma Guanhe, the former general manager of the telephone company, borrowed 420,000 Japanese yen from the company in the tenth year of the Republic, using the telephone company's machinery, land, and materials as collateral. In addition to repaying 20,000 Japanese yen on March 10th of the twelfth year and paying interest on November 3rd of the same year, the principal and interest have not been paid since then. They requested the court to order the defendants Ma Guanhe and the Jinan Telephone Company to jointly repay the principal and interest, and also requested provisional execution. After the District Court approved the request and issued a summons, Judge Fei Yinshou heard the case. Yesterday (the 28th), the court ruled that the telephone company should repay the Toyo Takushoku Kabushiki Kaisha a total of more than 600,000 Japanese yen in principal and interest, equivalent to more than 1 million yuan in national currency, and announced provisional execution. It is heard that the telephone company was unaware that Ma Guanhe borrowed money from the Japanese-owned Toyo Takushoku Kabushiki Kaisha. Although some directors signed the contract, it was handled solely by Ma Guanhe, and all the directors were unaware. When the company was reorganized, accountant Xie Lin checked all the accounts, and the 1.2 million yuan in debt included only the price of machinery from the German-owned Siemens foreign firm, and the remaining funds were loans from banks and firms in Jinan and Tianjin, with no interest-bearing loans from Japanese businessmen. Therefore, the occurrence of this incident was completely unexpected. Currently, in addition to declaring an appeal, the company is also submitting a request to the provincial government, municipal government, and the Department of Agriculture and Mines to preside over the matter on their behalf, and sending a letter to the court to revoke the provisional execution. At the same time, Ma Guanhe is ordered to appear in court to clarify the situation. All circles in commercial Jinan believe that this matter concerns China's transportation industry and cannot allow foreigners to encroach upon it, and are preparing to unanimously support it to protect sovereignty. (October 29)

Shi Yousan Passes Through Tianjin to Shenyang 83

Visiting Zhang Xueliang to Discuss Defense Matters

His Troops Concentrated Around Zhangde

Tianjin Correspondence: After Shi Yousan withdrew his troops to the northern section of the Pinghan Railway, he sent personnel to beg Zhang Xueliang and Han Fuju to intercede with the Central Government to allow him to surrender. Shi is a native of Jilin and has local ties to the Northeast, so Zhang Xueliang intends to promote him. It is heard that he has asked the Central Government to grant him the title of Commander-in-Chief. To show his sincerity to Zhang, Shi set off from Zhangde on the 21st and took a special train to Shenyang to meet with Zhang Xueliang. Before leaving, he telegraphed Zhang to explain his intention to visit, and Zhang telegraphed back to express his welcome. Shi then departed. His special train entered the Beining Railway at Changxindian, so it did not enter Beiping. It arrived in Tianjin at 6:00 AM today (the 23rd). Zhang Xueming, the director of the Tianjin Municipal Police Bureau, and Liu Hongru, the adjutant to Wang Shuchang, and Wang Dexin, the chief of the general staff, personally went to the station to welcome him. Those who came with Shi included Secretary-General Zhang Yunze and Bi Guangtan, the director of the Construction Department when Shi was the chairman of Shandong Province, Sun Tieling, a senator, as well as adjutants, staff officers, and hundreds of guards. Lin Jiaxun, the artillery commander of the army, took a special train as a pilot train, arriving in Tianjin half an hour before Shi. Qin Jianbin, whom Shi sent to Jinan to visit Han Fuju, also rushed from Jinan at about 11:00 AM to report on the negotiations. After getting off the train, Shi went to pay his respects to Wang Shuchang, Zhang Xueming, and other military and political figures, and went to his residence at No. 6 Road in the British Concession to rest. (This residence was the property of Li Sihao and was sold to Shi for 100,000 yuan.) Wang Shuchang hosted a banquet for Shi at 4:00 PM in the large reception hall of the provincial government to welcome him, and invited Shi's senior officers and Zhang Xueming, Zang Qifang, and others to accompany him. After the banquet, when interviewed, Shi stated that the purpose of his trip to the Northeast could be divided into two: first, because the Central Government ordered that all military affairs in the north be under the responsibility of Deputy Commander Zhang, and Zhang recently sent a telegram inviting him to meet, so he went to discuss the issue of defense zones; second, because his father was ill and he needed to return home to visit him. He planned to stay for about a week. His army is currently stationed in the area of Xinxiang, Weihui, Xunde, Zhangde, and Daokou, and a portion of it has been deployed to Daming, because there are miscellaneous troops such as Liu Guitang and Xue Chuanfeng causing disturbances in that area, so they were sent to protect local security. Liu and others have already fled elsewhere. The defense zone of his army is connected to the Northeast Army according to the orders of Deputy Commander Zhang. Currently, the area south of Zhangde is the responsibility of his army, and the area north of Zhangde is the responsibility of the Northeast Army's cavalry. A large portion of the Northeast Army has already arrived in Shijiazhuang. Lu Zhonglin is leading a large portion of the remnants of the Second Route Army in northern Henan, and a portion has entered southern Shanxi. Sun Lianzhong's troops are now in Jiaozuo, and Han Fuju is interceding with the Central Government to allow them to surrender. Since each unit is willing to submit to the Central Government at this time, they must wait for the Central Government to reorganize them, and most of them are in negotiations. He has not yet been appointed as Commander-in-Chief by the Central Government, but today he received a telegram from Deputy Commander Zhang saying that the Central Government has approved it. Because the telegram was encrypted, he was unable to translate it and does not know which route it is. His army currently has more than 60,000 men, 80% of whom have guns. Yan Xishan previously designated the three southern prefectures of Hebei for his army to raise funds, but the current situation has changed and it is only able to maintain supplies. Shi's special train left Tianjin for Shenyang at about 6:00 PM that afternoon. (October 23)

Northeast Unified Telecommunications Administration 84

Shenyang Correspondence: The Northeast Communications Committee, in order to implement unified administration, command, supervision, and inspection of telegraph, telephone, and radio communications within the provinces and regions of the Northeast, planned to organize a General Telecommunications Bureau in September of this year. However, it was not realized due to circumstances. Recently, after Zhu Guangmu took over as the director of the Administration Bureau, he presented the previous proposal to the Communications Committee for continued organization and implementation. The name of the Administration Bureau remains the same. The Communications Committee will establish a Northeast Telecommunications Administration Office directly under the Communications Committee. According to its organizational content, all current duties of the Telecommunications Administration Bureau and the Shenyang Telegraph, Telephone, and Radio Bureaus/Stations will be concurrently handled by the Northeast Telecommunications Administration Office. The original positions of Director of the Shenyang Telegraph Bureau, Director of the Provincial City Telephone Bureau, and Director of the Radio Station will all be abolished. A Chief of Operations will be established to handle the affairs of the bureaus and stations. All agencies under the jurisdiction of the Administration Office, all radio stations, all long-distance and city telephone bureaus, and telegraph bureaus within the Northeast region will be directly under it. The Administration Office will have a Director appointed by the Communications Committee. It is heard that Zhu Guangmu has been appointed to fill the position. The internal structure of the office is divided into four sections: General Affairs, Operations, Engineering, and Accounting. A Chief Engineer will also be established. The responsibilities of the office are roughly divided into the following items: (1) Matters concerning the appointment, removal, transfer, and evaluation of directors and branch directors of each bureau/station; (2) Matters concerning the evaluation of technical, reporting, and telephone staff; (3) Matters concerning the investigation of local military, political, industrial, and commercial conditions and whether to increase or abolish telecommunications bureaus/stations; (4) Matters concerning the investigation of reporting and telephone business conditions and whether to raise or lower the level of each bureau/station; (5) Matters concerning construction, improvement, or development plans; (6) Matters concerning the supervision of the income and expenditure of each bureau/station; (7) Matters concerning appeals and inquiries from local groups or merchants and contacts with local public affairs; (8) Matters concerning matters assigned by order. Regarding the above plan, the Communications Committee previously convened meetings with the Telecommunications Administration Bureau, the General Radio Station, the Provincial City Telegraph Bureau, the Shenyang Telephone Bureau, and other related parties to discuss the establishment of the Administration Office and the established organizational outline, and a general decision has been made. It is heard that it is scheduled to be established on the first of next month.

(October 24)

Local Sino-Russian Trade in Heihe 85

A Treaty Concluded by the Head of the Municipal Administration Office and the Russian Consul

To be Cancelled After the Promulgation of the Formal Sino-Russian Commercial Treaty

Harbin Correspondence: In June of this year, the Soviet Consul stationed in Heihe, Korniev, and Zhang Shouzeng, the head of the Heihe Municipal Preparatory Office, met in Heihe to discuss the issue of Sino-Russian international river navigation markers. At that time, the Russian Consul raised the issue of local trade in Heihe, requesting that both sides conclude a temporary local Sino-Russian commercial treaty in Heihe before the formal Sino-Russian commercial treaty was approved. Zhang, believing that the matter was of great importance, agreed to discuss it after the issue of navigation markers was resolved. However, the Soviet Far East has been suffering from food shortages in recent years and is in dire need of Chinese grain and groceries to provide relief, especially in the vicinity of Hailanpao. Therefore, after the issue of international river navigation markers was resolved, the Russian Consul raised the issue of trade again. Zhang Shouzeng reported the situation to the Heilongjiang Provincial Government, which in turn reported it to the Northeast Political Affairs Committee. The Central Government telegraphed back a month ago, believing that since the Sino-Soviet Conference had already opened, local trade could be opened to show generosity if it did not harm national sovereignty, and instructed the Northeast side to consider it. The Political Affairs Committee, in accordance with this instruction, ordered Zhang Shouzeng to consult with the Russian Consul in Heihe in good faith, ensuring that it did not violate the general Sino-Russian treaty. Although a temporary treaty has been concluded, it must be revoked when the formal Sino-Russian commercial treaty is approved. On the 19th of this month, Zhang Shouzeng and the Russian Consul in Heihe agreed on a full treaty consisting of eleven articles and have submitted it to the highest authorities of both China and Russia for approval. The Russian side has recently been preparing to establish a state-owned commercial representative office and other commercial institutions in Heihe. Chinese officials and merchants in Heihe have also raised 100,000 yuan to establish the Northeast Trading Company. It is expected that the development of Sino-Russian commerce will begin after the treaty is approved. Heihe has been extremely desolate in recent years. If local trade is allowed, it may return to prosperity. (October 22)

CER to Establish Translation Office 86

To be Established on November 1

Russians Have Deep Intentions to Manipulate

Harbin Correspondence: The Chinese Eastern Railway (CER) Translation Office, decided by Russian Director Rufaev, has appointed Wu Hongyou, Chief of the General Affairs Department, Cai Yunchang, Chief of the Sino-Russian Secretariat, Sun Yutang, Director of Translation, and Russian Directors Niechieff, Yacoulev, and Krimiankoff as preparatory committee members. They are required to report the preparation situation to the Director by the 27th of this month so that it can be formally established on the 1st of next month. Cai Yunchang, the Chief of the Sino-Russian Secretariat, will be transferred to be the director of the office, but the formal and deputy titles have not yet been determined. After the Translation Office is established, the original Sino-Russian Secretariat and the Translation Section of the General Affairs Department will be merged into it. All personnel will also be transferred to serve in the office. However, the name of the Translation Office is directly translated from Russian, which the Chinese side considers inappropriate. Therefore, it is planned that the preparatory committee will submit the regulations to the Council for approval so that they can be determined. The initial intention of the Russian Director was to establish the Translation Office on October 1. However, the Chinese directors unanimously opposed it, believing that once the translators from each department were transferred to serve in the Translation Office, it would be inconvenient for each department to handle affairs. Therefore, they requested a delay in the establishment. After a second study by the Chinese and Russian Councilors, it was approved that each department would retain two or three translators to serve in their own department, while the rest would be transferred to serve in the Translation Office. The Chinese directors, realizing that it was impossible to fundamentally overturn the decision, stopped opposing it. Therefore, the Russian Director ordered that the Translation Office be organized and established on November 1. The internal structure of the Translation Office is roughly divided into four sections: Technical, Document, Literary, and Accounting. The annual expenditure of the entire office is 5 million rubles, and there are approximately 100 employees. The Russian Director initially expected that the Russian directors would also oppose this proposal at the board meeting. However, at the second meeting, they all changed their attitude and unanimously supported it. Therefore, some researchers have made a thorough study of the key to this. After a certain Chinese director discovered it, it was believed that the Russian side wanted to restrict the Chinese side's use of personnel and control the affairs of each department, so they concentrated the translation talents to invisibly resist this. This is because the Russian side knows that the Chinese side lacks specialized technical talents, so they use this strategy. (October 22)

Zhang Lisheng's Troops to Undergo Inspection 87

Bengbu Correspondence: Zhang Lisheng, the commander of the Cavalry Group Army and the commander of the Second Cavalry Division, since concurrently serving as the Road Protection Commander of the Pupu section of the Jinpu Line, his troops, except for the Eighth and Eleventh Regiments stationed in eastern Henan, are all distributed in the southern section of the Jinpu Line, responsible for road protection and bandit suppression. Recent News from the Guizhou Scientific Survey Team of the Academia Sinica 88

Since its establishment, the National Museum of Natural History of the Academia Sinica has spared no effort in its work. In addition to continuously studying the various specimens obtained in Guangxi in previous years and publishing them in the museum's journal, Sinensia, it has also conducted detailed collections near Beijing. Last year, it sent personnel to Sichuan to collect animals, with excellent results. Because the animals and plants in Guizhou Province have not been thoroughly investigated by domestic and foreign experts, the museum specially organized a Guizhou Natural Science Survey Team this year, dividing it into animal and plant groups. Chang Linding, Tang Ruijin, Fang Zilian, and Tang Kaipin were assigned as animal group investigators, Jiang Ying and Huang Zhi as plant group investigators, and Lin Yingshi as secretary, stationed in Guiyang to manage rear affairs. After the organization was completed, it departed from Beijing on April 11, passed through Chongqing, Sichuan, and arrived in Tongzi County in northern Guizhou Province on May 12 and began the investigation. A large number of animal and plant specimens were collected in the Loushan Pass area. It arrived in Zunyi County in the south and investigated for half a month before arriving in Guiyang on June 13 and staying at the provincial government's reception center in Zhongshan Park. Chairman Mao and the heads of various departments held a banquet to welcome the team. After resting briefly in the province, the team formulated a route and set off in two teams for investigation. One team went west to counties such as Dingfan, Guangshun, Pingba, Xiuwen, Qianxi, Dading, Bijie, Weining, and Shuicheng. The other team went east to counties such as Longli, Guiding, Duyun, Maha, and Bazhai, and then turned south to counties such as Sanhe, Libo, and Dushan, and then along the west to counties such as Pingzhou, Datang, and Luohue. In the four months since the investigation began, the plant group has obtained many kinds of medicinal materials, fungi, and timber, and collected more than 4,000 numbers of plant specimens, totaling about 60,000 to 70,000 copies. The animal group obtained more than 1,600 pairs of birds, totaling more than 180 species, more than 2,000 fish, totaling more than 150 species, amphibians, reptiles, mammals, etc., totaling more than 80 species, totaling more than 200 copies, and more than 4,000 pieces of invertebrates. In addition, it also obtained live animals such as civet cats, otters, yellow muntjacs, monkeys, bears, pigs, and badgers. It is heard that the team is still continuing its investigation and is expected to return to Beijing at the end of February next year.

Ministry of Communications Restricts Additions to Wuxi-Liyang Shipping Route: Several river steamer companies, including the Wuxi Merchants' Shipping Company, China Merchants, Yonggu New Shipping, and others, noted that since the Wuxi-Liyang route began operating, there have been as many as four round trips per day, leading to an oversupply. They jointly requested the Shipping Association to forward a petition to the Ministry of Communications to restrict the addition of vessels on the Wuxi-Liyang route to avoid disputes and benefit shipping. Yesterday, Directive No. 4522 from the Ministry of Communications was received, stating that since there was no need to add vessels to the route, the established case should be followed and additions restricted. As for the Tongyu Company's request to the Changshu and Wuxi county governments for the issuance of notices to rescind the restriction, a response should be issued after receiving an order from the Jiangsu Construction Bureau to have the counties investigate before further review.

Monks Appeal for the Return of Chong'an Temple: The Grand Hall of the Great Hero of Chong'an Temple in the city of Wuxi is an ancient temple from the Jin Dynasty. The former abbot, Longzhi, reported to the county and was issued a license to manage the temple and pay taxes, and it was entirely the private property of the monks. Last autumn, the county police headquarters was moved into the hall by former County Magistrate Sun and has been stationed there for over a year. Recently, the police headquarters moved to the Yanshou Si Hall outside the East Gate. Therefore, yesterday, retired monk Songyun, Jialiang, the abbot of Zhongyin Temple, Liangru, the abbot of Bao'an Temple, Rongting, the abbot of Nanyuan Temple, Hongpei of the Yaoshi Hermitage, Yanchi of the Ren Cao Hermitage, retired monk Puqing, and abbots of various temples, totaling fourteen people, jointly submitted a petition to the county government, requesting permission to return the temple to the monks for management in accordance with temple regulations and to preserve historical sites.

Imposter Exposed and Arrested: At the Liangxi Inn on Tongyun Road outside the Guangfu Gate in Wuxi, six people from Hubei Province, including Xiang Chongkai, Wang Bingxun, Xiang Renfa, Feng Futian, Huang Mingjue, and Xiang Zhenyi, were staying in room number 19. Xiang Chongkai, who appeared to be around forty years old, wore a long gown and mandarin jacket and behaved in a generous manner. He claimed to have been commissioned by the provincial government as the Director of the Wuxi Municipal Public Security Bureau. The day before yesterday, he fabricated a telegram and sent someone to Zhenjiang to have it telegraphed. The telegram was addressed to Xu Jigui, the Director of the Wuxi County Public Security Bureau, and was signed by Ye Chucang, the Chairman of the Provincial Government. The telegram stated that Xiang Chongkai was a loyal and capable person and should be given a job. Director Xu received the telegram and reasoned that since there was no municipal government established in Wuxi, there could not be a Municipal Public Security Bureau Director, and that if Chairman Ye were to recommend someone, he would first contact County Magistrate Pan and would not directly telegraph him. Director Xu immediately took the telegram to County Magistrate Pan for instructions. Pan also found the telegram to be suspicious and ordered Director Xu to telegraph Chairman Ye for instructions. He received a reply stating that there was no such matter and ordered him to send someone to arrest Xiang. After receiving the telegram, Director Xu secretly dispatched Detective Team Leader Shen Minhua and Detective Tang Yaoting to room 19 of the Liangxi Inn. They first tricked Xiang Chongkai into going to the bureau and placed him under strict surveillance. Then, they returned to the inn and arrested Wang Bingxun, Xiang Renfa, Feng Futian, Huang Mingjue, and Xiang Zhenyi. Yesterday afternoon at 4 PM, Wang Zhonghu, the head of the Third Section, opened the court for interrogation. Because the case involved impersonating a high-ranking official and forging documents, he ordered them to be detained pending transfer to the county government for legal proceedings.

Qingpu 92

Private Settlement of Homicide Case to Be Thoroughly Investigated: A certain Mrs. Cao, a woman from the Cao family near Yandian Bridge in Baihejiang Town in this county, died from serious injuries the day before yesterday due to a quarrel with her family. The local guarantor, Zhu Jingbai, did not report the case to the authorities for inspection. Instead, the Cao family paid 600 yuan to settle the matter privately. It is now heard that the authorities have discovered this and will conduct a thorough investigation.

Three Bandits Executed by Firing Squad: The county government previously received five bandits, Zhu Sanmao, Fan Youxing, Chen Ajinmao, Gu Deqin, and Gao Da, who were escorted by the water patrol. After repeated interrogations, it was determined that Gu Deqin and Gao Da were forced by the bandits to row the boat and their involvement was relatively minor, so they would be dealt with separately. Zhu Sanmao, Fan Youxing, and Chen Ajinmao confessed to the kidnapping and robbery cases of Yao Chang in Qitangtou and Cao Aliuliu in Shengjiawan. They were sentenced to death and the provincial government approved the execution. The execution was carried out by firing squad at the execution ground at 7 AM the day before yesterday after confirming the identities of the convicts.

Changshu 93

Resignation of Water Police 13th Squad Leader: Yang Qingjiu, the leader of the 13th squad of the 3rd district of the water police, has been stationed in Changshu for more than six years and is quite familiar with the local people and situation. Recently, Gong Guozhen, the leader of the 3rd district, resigned and Shen Gaozhen was appointed by the province to succeed him. Squad Leader Yang felt that since District Leader Shen had plans for reorganization, he would be unable to continue his duties and submitted a report to District Leader Shen requesting to be relieved of his position. This was heard by the district leaders in Changshu, who, recognizing Squad Leader Yang's repeated efforts in suppressing bandits and his meritorious service, jointly telegraphed the provincial government and the Civil Affairs Department, led by Wu Xinheng, the leader of the 1st district, to unanimously retain him.

Four Generations of Township Head's Family Kidnapped: The family of Qu Shangzhen, the head of Changyan Township, Nianbu Bridge, Dongwu District, in this county, was suddenly attacked at 12 o'clock the night before last by more than 40 sea bandits. They landed at Gaopukou and swarmed to the house, first surrounding the residence and then using stone bars to break open the front and back doors. They entered and looted, then kidnapped five members of the household. Township Head Qu Shangzhen, who is 67 years old, was only wearing his upper garment when he was kidnapped. His son, Genfu, who is 35 years old, was bedridden and could not walk, so he was carried away by the bandits. His daughter-in-law, Wang, is 28 years old, his nephew's daughter-in-law, Xia, and his great-nephew, Chunshi, is 8 years old. Only his wife, Xuan, was spared. According to Xuan, the bandits lit candles to illuminate the entire house and were wearing grey clothes, some with copper-rimmed felt hats. They each held box cannons and looted for about an hour, then took the loot and hostages and boarded a boat towards the riverbank. Before leaving, they fired several box cannons. It was also heard that the bandits had first gone to the house of Lu Xincheng, the head of Nianbu Bridge Township, but the occupants escaped after hearing the noise. The bandits only looted valuables and all the family members were safe.

Jiangyin 94

Chamber of Commerce Submits Opinions on Using Business Tax to Offset Likin Abolition: Zhu Danqing, chairman of the preparatory committee of the county chamber of commerce, submitted opinions on using business tax to offset likin abolition to the National Government Executive Yuan and the finance and commerce departments to eliminate future obstacles to the business tax and promote benefits. The original text is very long. The following is an outline: (1) Business license registration can only be implemented after the abolition of likin. (2) Abolish inland regular customs, as they are similar to likin in nature. (3) Abolish all special tax bureaus, as they originally came from the commodity tax. (4) Do not set up inspection agencies to avoid various demands. (5) After the implementation of the business tax, taxes should be levied uniformly according to the amount of capital. Those with capital less than 500 yuan may be exempted to show consideration for small businesses.

Telegram Requesting Cancellation of Fabric Relief Donation: Wu Shouying, chairman of the Jiangyin Fabric Trade Association, stated that in August of the twelfth year of the Republic of China, there were disasters and famines in Jingzhao, Zhili, and Gan provinces. At that time, the former Beijing Ministry of Finance issued an order to add 20% to commodity taxes for relief donations, which were originally scheduled to be abolished in June. At that time, the fabric tax was collected by the tax office. However, when the June deadline passed, it was not stopped and continued year after year, creating an unbearable extra burden. Yesterday, a special telegram was sent to the Executive Yuan, the provincial government, and the Ministry of Finance, requesting them to order the cancellation and submit it to the county council for forwarding to the central government, and to telegraph all counties to unanimously advocate for the relief of business difficulties.

Telegram Urging Wang Jiajin, Wang Guozuo, etc., to Hand Over: Shen Lunxu, director of the Finance Bureau, stated that the handover from the two former county magistrates, Wang Jiajin and Wang Guozuo, had been prepared and sent several times, and letters had been sent to urge them to meet and settle accounts, but they had not yet come to clarify the matter. Now, a special telegram has been sent to the Finance Department to disclose that Wang Jiajin's original residence is Lishui County, and Wang Guozuo's original residence is the Mianshi Street of Ganzhou, Jiangxi. The Wang Jucai of Wang Juyitai shop should be instructed to order the local officials of their original residences to order them to come to Cheng as soon as possible to settle accounts in order to complete the formalities.

Nantong 95

The Bandit Case in Pingchao District Expands: Wu Qinmian and Yang Jinyun, bandits captured in Pingchao District, were borrowed from the county court by the county government for investigation and were released. This caused a public outcry. The two bandits, Wu and Yang, have now been captured by the county government. Instructions have been requested from the province for punishment. An emergency meeting was held in Pingchao. A telegram accusing Prosecutor Zhu of the court was sent. The telegram read: "To Court President Bei and Chief Prosecutor Wang Junjian of the Nantong County Court. The Nantong County Court Prosecutor's Office secretly released well-known communist bandits Wu Qinmin and Yang Jinyun this month. The judiciary is dark and the public is indignant. In addition to telegraphed reports to the Provincial Government Security Office and the Civil Affairs Department, we implore you to send personnel to conduct a thorough investigation and strict inquiry." The telegrams to the province and other departments were similar and are omitted.

Severely Punish the Illegal County Police Captain: Yan Diannan, the former captain of the Nantong County Police Brigade, was corrupt and lawless during his tenure. After being accused by the people, he was arrested in Bengbu. He is now detained in the Zhenjiang County Prison Detention Center. The province ordered the county to send the evidence in the case for review in order to severely punish him.

Difficulties in Tax Collection at Salt Fields: The collection of taxes from the salt fields in Tongru has always been handled by the field office. Currently, bandits are rampant, and the field police have not yet been formed. Tax collectors are sometimes harmed by bandits. The field chiefs have reported the difficulties to Zhang, the salt commissioner of the Lianghuai Salt Transport Department, who consulted the provincial government and ordered the county magistrates of Tongru to send police to assist.

Deadline to Hand Over Rent Income from Zhang Qian's Confiscated Property: The rent income from Zhang Qian's confiscated property, which has been used by the local government for a considerable amount, has been ordered by the provincial government to be returned to the province by the end of this month. Fundraising Measures for the Relief Institute: The fundraising methods required to establish the relief institute in Tongyi were resolved by representatives of various groups at a meeting to collect additional fees on flour, sesame cakes, and other items.

Zhenjiang 96

Details of the Fuyun-Fengyu Steamer Sinking After Being Attacked by Bandits: It is not uncommon for small inland steamers to be robbed by bandits. Although the various steamer companies have repeatedly petitioned the competent authorities to strictly prevent banditry, the bandits are still rampant, and travelers have lost their security and are wary. At 9:30 AM on the 28th, the Fengyu steamer of the Fuyun Steamer Company, towing the Fuan tugboat, departed from Zhenjiang for Baoying. At around 6:00 PM, after passing the Zhaoguan Dam dock for about six or seven li, while proceeding under power, suddenly dozens of bandits were spotted on the shore, firing a volley and ordering the ship to stop. The captain, seeing the ferocity of the bandits, stopped the ship and docked, but the hull had been pierced by a bullet and water poured in, causing the ship to sink immediately. Fortunately, all the passengers were on the tugboat and were not submerged. After boarding the tugboat, the bandits robbed the passengers of their silver, clothing, luggage, and other items, and then fled. In order to protect the safety of passengers, the inland steamer companies had been approved by the competent authorities in June to send police to protect the ships. There were twelve water police officers on board that day, protecting the high officials in the cabins. When the bandits attempted to rob and opened fire, the police officers remained in the cabins and did not resist, and all their guns were confiscated by the bandits. A water police officer from the Sixth District was wounded by a bullet that grazed his mouth and shoulder. He was taken to the provincial hospital in Zhenjiang by another steamer. According to the passengers who were victimized, the injured police officer had inspected the passengers after the ship left Zhenjiang and found a bandit with contraband. The bandit harbored resentment and retaliated later. After the ship passed Zhaoguan Dam for six or seven li, the bandits hiding on the ship fired shots and signaled to the bandits on the shore, firing shots to deter the police on board. A cook named Li Xiaowuzi and a female passenger were killed by the bullets. When the company's Qingjiang steamer heading upstream arrived at the scene, the passengers cried for help. The Qingjiang steamer towed the tugboat to Baoying, and the bodies of those killed by the bandits were sent to the Shaobo Steamer Bureau. Yesterday, after receiving a telephone report, the company sent legal counsel Tao Gongwu and public relations director Tao Shoubo on a special steamer to investigate the truth and report to the Yangzhou court, requesting it to send personnel to examine the bodies. They also reported the incident to the Shipping Association, requesting it to forward the report to the authorities for strict investigation. It is heard that the association telegraphed the Ministry of Communications yesterday after receiving the report.

Appointment of Agricultural Association Reorganization Committee Members in Nine Counties: The Jiangsu Provincial Party Reorganization Committee yesterday appointed members to reorganize the farmers' associations in nine counties, including Kunshan. The list is as follows: (Kunshan) Fang Touxia, Wang Zhenhuan, Yang Qingrong; (Wujiang) Mei Fulin, Zhu Boyi, Wang Liao Wei; (Yixing) Lu Rongquan, Pan Zhisheng, Jiang Maolin; (Qidong) Zhu Chunwan, Zhu Yuxiu, Zhang Xiefeng; (Liyang) Rui Zhenxiang, Jiang Wei, Yang Jiaxiang; (Jiangpu) Li Rongtang, Zhao Shiying, Tang Shiyi; (Taixing) Ji Shaozong, Zhang Yuxiu, Lu Rui; (Taicang) Pu Danan, Zhu Fuli, Lu Zuolin; (Huai'an) Wu Yuren, Liu Xi, Qiao Mosheng.

Qidong County Telegram for Arrest of Former County Magistrate: Xia Yueqing, the former county magistrate of Qidong County, was dismissed from his post due to a case. The Civil Affairs Department had appointed Zhou Lansheng to replace him. However, after receiving the provincial order, County Magistrate Xia knew that his crimes were serious and he would likely be unable to avoid punishment. The day before yesterday, he hired a car and attempted to flee secretly. He was stopped by the public and the police, but he managed to bribe various agencies to release him. The public refused to allow this. In desperation, Xia forcibly ordered the car to leave early on the 24th and fled secretly. Various circles then ordered the police to pursue and detain him, but they were unsuccessful. Yesterday, a public telegram was sent to the provincial government to strictly arrest him and hold him accountable.

The Construction Department Strictly Prohibits Banquets and Empty Formalities: The Construction Department recently announced that banquets and empty formalities by public officials have long been strictly prohibited. However, it has been found that the heads of the construction bureaus in various counties often send invitations to the officials of the department for banquets after completing their official business in the province, in order to establish connections. This inevitably falls into bad habits and uses the wealth of one person to provide food for many. Such meaningless socializing wastes both time and money. Yesterday, a clear order was issued to warn against this.

Yangzhou 97

Shaoxing 99

Looting and Robbery of Police Weapons During Shuangjiangxi Festival: Wangtan, Qingtan, and other places in Lishan Village, Ping Shui in Shaoxing, have recently been holding a God-welcoming festival at the Shuangjiangxi River, which is near the border of Shaoxing and Sheng counties. Many people from the three counties of Shaoxing, Sheng, and Zhuji have joined in the festivities. As a result, bandits from Sheng seized the opportunity to mingle in the crowd. On the morning of the 29th, dozens of bandits armed with wooden-cased guns rose up and robbed the Wangtan Substation, taking five patrol officers and police officers hostage and stealing their weapons. They also kidnapped the owner and shop assistants of the Tao Xing Hao shop and demanded a large ransom. The Public Security Bureau, after hearing the news, has sent a team to pursue them.

Request to the Province to Quickly Repair Qianjiang Ferry: The Qianjiang ferry in this province has a total of eight tugboats that travel back and forth, which is still insufficient. Recently, half of them have been ashore awaiting repairs, but they have not progressed for half a year, causing traffic delays. Yesterday, the county executive committee resolved to submit a request to the provincial executive committee to forward a letter to the provincial government, ordering the swift repair of the ships awaiting repair and to allocate funds to purchase tugboats.

Letter from Guangzhou Provincial Government 101

Dear Sirs, According to a letter from Yun Daqi, the former Section Chief of the Third Section of the Secretariat of this government, he read in the domestic news section of the Shanghai Shen Bao on October 8 that a telegram from Hong Kong stated that the Guangdong authorities were strictly arresting Yun Daqi and several others. He was very surprised because Daqi has been reading behind closed doors lately and has not been involved in external affairs. Apart from family letters, he has not corresponded with any relatives or friends. He believes that he has not committed any public or private offenses that would warrant the authorities' strict arrest. Therefore, he requests that your government inform the newspaper to make appropriate corrections to clarify the truth. In this regard, this government has not issued such an arrest warrant and the matters presented in the letter are true. Therefore, we specifically request your newspaper to immediately correct the aforementioned telegram. The Guangdong Provincial Government, October 21, 19th year of the Republic of China

Education Department Advisor Chen Temporarily Continues to Serve Concurrently as Director 103

Chen Shizhen, an advisor to the Ministry of Education, previously requested to be relieved of his concurrent position as Director. On the 9th, the Ministry of Education ordered the advisor to relinquish his concurrent position as Director of the Department of Social Affairs only when Yang Lian arrives at the ministry. The original instruction said, "We have been informed that the advisor has been meticulous in his work since taking office and is deeply respected. Because Director Chen Liu resigned, a successor could not be found for a time, so the advisor was temporarily requested to serve concurrently as the Director of the Department of Social Education, which increased the workload and made him more diligent. Later, Chen repeatedly stated that his health was weak and it was difficult to handle both the advisor and director positions, and his request was sincere. After submitting it to the Executive Yuan for review and submitting it to the National Government, Yang Lian was appointed as the Director of the Department of Social Education of this ministry and the advisor should relinquish the concurrent position of director only after the director arrives at the ministry. We hope that you will continue to persevere and maintain the highest standards."

Ministry of Education Explains the Personnel Appointment Methods for Social Education 104

The Ministry of Education instructed the Jiangsu Education Department to explain the doubts raised by the department regarding the personnel appointment methods for the directors of county-level social education institutions. The instruction read, "We have been informed that the social education institutions mentioned in Order No. 445 of the Ministry of Education, which was issued to the provinces, cities, and counties regarding the appointment and removal methods for principals of secondary schools and directors of social education institutions, refer to those with a larger scale, such as education halls, museums, art galleries, libraries, public stadiums, etc., which are already noted in the parentheses of Article 1. The reading rooms, literacy centers, inquiry centers, and public teahouses mentioned in the report have simple organizations and are small-scale social education institutions and are not included. The appointment and removal of their directors are not subject to the aforementioned methods established by the Ministry. The local educational administrative agencies should establish separate regulations for compliance. The appointment procedures for principals of public schools have been clearly stipulated in Article 13 of the Outline of Public School Methods promulgated by the Ministry. Please comply accordingly."

The Ministry of Education Again Petitions the Central Government to Abolish the Sino-Japanese Cultural Agreement 105

The Sino-Japanese Cultural Agreement is a tool for Japan's cultural aggression against China. The Ministry of Education previously listed the inappropriateness of this agreement, drafted a plan to abolish the Sino-Japanese Cultural Agreement, and submitted it to the Central Government to negotiate with Japan for its abolition. At the same time, it ordered the Chinese members of the Sino-Japanese Cultural Undertakings Foundation Committee to withdraw from the committee, and notified the Supervision Office for Students Studying in Japan to stop subsidizing tuition fees issued by the Japanese Cultural Affairs Bureau in China, to demonstrate its firm opposition to the Sino-Japanese Cultural Agreement. This stance has been repeatedly reported in this newspaper. The contents of the plan to abolish the Sino-Japanese Cultural Agreement drafted by the Ministry of Education (the contents of the plan are confidential diplomatic documents and will not be published for the time being) are, according to inquiries, roughly divided into two measures: (1) Japan's Boxer Indemnity should be fully returned to China and freely used by China for the development of Sino-Japanese cultural undertakings; (2) The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Cultural Affairs Bureau in China should be abolished, and a new organization should be jointly established by China and Japan to handle Sino-Japanese cultural undertakings based on the principle of equality, and the scope of cultural undertakings should be defined, etc. After the Central Political Conference deliberated on the plan, it was submitted to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with Japan. Recently, a reply was received from Japan, completely disagreeing with the first measure of the plan, and only agreeing to change the method of subsidizing tuition fees for Chinese students studying in Japan for the second measure, while insisting on the original terms of the cultural agreement. Yesterday, the Ministry of Education refuted the points of Japan's reply and again stated the impropriety of the agreement's contents, submitting a second petition to the Central Government to lodge a serious protest with the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs. The summary and annotations of the Sino-Japanese Cultural Agreement issued by the Ministry of Education are recorded below: (1) When Japan is conducting cultural affairs in China, it should fully respect the opinions of the representatives of the uneducated classes in China (Article 1). (2) The funds under the Boxer Indemnity shall be mainly used for cultural undertakings run by Chinese people. As for the schools, hospitals, and other cultural undertakings currently operated by Japanese groups in China in Shandong, the subsidy funds shall be specifically drawn from the funds under the Shandong Indemnity. (3) Libraries and institutes of spiritual science shall be established in Beijing, and the land shall be allocated by the Chinese government free of charge. Natural science institutes shall be established in Shanghai, and museums shall be established in suitable locations if there are surplus funds. Medical universities shall be established in Jinan, affiliated with Jinan hospitals. Medical schools and affiliated hospitals shall be established in Guangdong (Articles 3, 4, 5, 6, 8). (4) Each of the aforementioned undertakings shall establish a council composed of Chinese and Japanese people, with approximately twenty members for each council, ten from each side, and an additional Chinese person selected through consultation between the two sides as the chairman (Article 7). (5) From the following year (fixed for ten years), tuition fees shall be granted to Chinese students studying in Japan according to the following methods: (A) 80 yuan per person per month; (B) Not exceeding 320 people; (C) The number shall be allocated to each province based on the number of representatives in the provincial assembly and the amount of Boxer Indemnity borne by each province, and selected from students studying at universities and specialized schools; these universities and specialized schools shall be designated through consultation between the Chinese ambassador to Japan and the Japanese Ministry of Education and the Cultural Affairs Bureau in China; (D) The selection of students shall not be limited to government-funded students, and self-funded students shall also be included; (E) Students who have already been selected may have their tuition fees stopped at any time if they are deemed to have poor academic performance or bad conduct (Draft Article 10, deleted and revised when formally signed). From the above agreement, it can be generally seen that the so-called handling of Chinese cultural undertakings is under the jurisdiction of the Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Cultural Affairs Bureau in China and is a part of Japan's internal affairs. The tuition subsidies for Chinese students studying in Japan within Japan are directly under the command of the Cultural Affairs Bureau in China, and are handled by the Chinese institutions managing students studying in Japan. Within China, cultural and charitable undertakings are handled by people dispatched by the Japanese government and entrusted to people dispatched by the Chinese government to assist in the handling, and the undertakings carried out within China can obtain the ownership of Chinese land. The so-called return of the Boxer Indemnity is actually the designation by the Japanese government accounting for certain revenue for certain internal affairs purposes, which is nothing more than cultural aggression against China.

Party Teachers Registration is Only Today 108

In the future, whether it is inspecting Party teaching in various schools or reviewing and verifying qualifications, it will be relevant. Therefore, qualified Party Doctrine teachers and training directors who are teaching in this city or intend to teach must complete the registration (with a photo). Those who are registered in other places and reside in this city should also report their departure to the original registering Party Headquarters in accordance with the law, fill in the Party Doctrine Teacher Transfer Certificate, and report to the Training Department of this city with a recent photo for registration. Because this registration is nothing less than a national general survey, every certified Party Doctrine teacher must complete the procedures for reporting departure and arrival in accordance with the law each time they arrive at a place, and register with the Party Headquarters at the place of arrival to clarify their relationship with the Party Headquarters at the place of arrival. For those who are certified in this city but have not yet registered, the City Training Department has a roster to check and will publish the names in the newspaper tomorrow, publicly summoning them to register within a time limit. Otherwise, after being found out, they will be reported to the Central Government for punishment.

Revisions to the Basketball Rules for 1930-1931 111

The basketball rules for 1930-1931 have been revised by the Far Eastern Games. The Chinese Referee Committee has translated them and added annotations to make them more noticeable. The revisions are recorded below:

First Revision of Rule 4 Add the following note: "An area can be designated on both sides of the free throw area line to assist in placing dual players during free throws. This area should be marked with the words 'Home' and 'Guest' to indicate the position that players from the home and visiting teams should take." (As shown in the figure, draw a short line five feet inside from the end line and write the words on the ground. One player from the home team and one player from the visiting team stand in this area. The remaining players stand alternately based on these two players, with the guest team next to the home team and the home team next to the guest team, so that the forces on both sides are balanced to avoid mutual competition for position. However, this is only a suggestion and is not required by the rules.)

Rule 1 of Article 4 The circumference of the ball shall be changed from 30 to 32 inches to 30 to 21 inches. The weight of the ball shall be changed from 20 to 23 ounces to 20 to 22 ounces.

Rule 3 of Article 5 Add "A player who is replaced by another player shall not immediately enter the game as a substitute before the game is temporarily suspended and restarted." (That is, if a player has been formally replaced and the game has not yet restarted, but suddenly wants to rejoin and replace another player, the recorder and referee may refuse the substitution. However, if the game has proceeded as usual after the substitution, even if it is only for a short time, and the player re-enters the field as a substitute to replace another player, it is still qualified.)

Rule 6 of Article 5 Add the phrase "or combined numbers that are easy to confuse viewers" after the note. (The ball number itself had a suggestion to avoid the numbers "1" and "2," but combined numbers are quite inconvenient for the referee to inspect and announce, hence this move.)

Rule 3 of Article 7 Add the following note: "If a player holding the ball near the boundary line is defended by an opponent within one yard and cannot attack, and holds the ball for more than five seconds, the referee may declare a 'jump ball.'" (If a player is forced into a corner and has no chance to turn or pass the ball, and holds the ball to wait for more than five seconds, the referee can declare a jump ball even if the opponent's hand has not touched the ball, in order to avoid wasting time. However, it should be noted that this rule only applies to situations where the player only has one side that can move and is blocked by the opponent. If it is in the middle of the field, both sides have opportunities to move, and this rule is not applicable.)

Rule 6 of Article 8 Revise the number of dribbles to "During a jump ball, the jumper may dribble the ball twice, but not more than two times. The second dribble does not necessarily have to be within the circle, it can also be outside the circle. After the second dribble, the jumper should not touch the ball until the ball has touched the other eight players, or the floor, or the basket, or the backboard." (According to the old rules, the number of dribbles was not clearly specified, and it had to be dribbled within the circle to make the ball dribble out of the circle. This rule allows the player to dribble out of the circle or dribble once again while still in the circle, which is more active than before.)

Rule 3 of Article 9 Add the following note: "In competitions for junior high or younger children, if the score is still tied after the first overtime period and it is necessary to extend the game again, there must be a five-minute rest period, and the players may leave the field during this rest period. However, the number of times of leaving the field during overtime is limited to three. During the second and third times, a one-minute rest period is still allowed, and they may not leave the field." (If the game is still tied at the end of the second overtime period, the coaches and captains of both sides should first agree on a method so that even if the score is equal in the third overtime period, a winner can be determined. The common method is to declare the team that first scores two points in the third overtime period as the winner, but each competent authority can stipulate it according to its own suitability. As for the case where the scores of both sides are obviously high after the third overtime, the winner is naturally judged based on the number of points, and it is no longer necessary to use the standard of first scoring two points.)

Rule 1 of Article 10 Add a referee note as follows: "The official's judgment on the ball going out of bounds should be very clear so that both sides do not misunderstand. If a misunderstanding unfortunately occurs, the official should take the ball in hand until both sides have the opportunity to restore their offensive and defensive positions, and then hand it over to the thrower. However, the official does not need to personally hand the ball to the thrower every time the ball goes out of bounds."

Rule 1 of Article 11 In the case of an infringement foul, the "time-out" should last from the time the foul occurs until the ball leaves the hand of the free thrower. If there are two or more consecutive free throws, then it should last until the last time the ball leaves the hand. Technical fouls and double fouls still last from the time the foul occurs until the jump ball in the center circle.

Rule 6 of Article 13 Delete the last sentence of the first paragraph of this rule to conform to the changes in the penalty for throwing the ball out of bounds.

Penalty for Rule 7 of Article 14 Revise to "If a free throw is awarded due to a technical foul, the free throw shall be taken in the center circle instead of at the nearest free throw line if the thrower steps out of the free throw line or his teammate enters the free throw area before the ball touches the basket or the backboard." (Because the success or failure of throwing the ball after a technical foul must be a jump ball in the center circle, it would contradict the ordinary free throw rules if the jump ball were still held on the free throw line according to the old rules, hence this revision.)

Rule 8 of Article 14 Add the following note: "Kicking the ball must be intentional to be punished. Unintentional clearing of the ball with the legs or feet is not a violation." (It is not easy to judge whether the kicking of the ball is intentional or unintentional, but the official's judgment based on the situation is better than not asking the reason and only regarding the contact between the ball and the leg as a violation, which would cause unnecessary obstacles to the game.) Subsection E of Rule 1 of Article 15 If a jumper leaves the circle before dribbling the ball during a jump ball, the penalty is changed from a violation to a technical foul, but if the ball is properly dribbled into its own basket in the circle by another jumper at this time, the ball is still valid, and the offender can be ignored. (Do not damage the interests already obtained by the non-offending party due to the foul, and consider the ball invalid and stuck in the free throw.)

Penalty for Infringement Foul in Article 15 If an infringement foul occurs while throwing the ball into the basket and the ball still hits the basket, add one free throw; if the ball fails to hit the basket as a result, award two free throws; if the second ball fails to hit the basket during the continuation of the game after the first free throw fails, continue the game (According to last year's revision, if a foul occurred and the ball still did not hit the basket, two free throws were awarded, but the jump ball in the center circle for whether the second ball hit or did not hit contradicted the ordinary free throw rules. This method is now revised to conform to the free throw rules. If one free throw fails, it is possible to score four consecutive points if one goal is scored to continue the game, which is still equal in value to the previous two free throws and is more fair than the two free throws that can stably score four points.)

The Jiangnan Association Football Tournament Will Be Held 115

The Jiangnan University Sports Association Football Standing Committee held a meeting at the Chinese National Sports Association on October 26 and decided on the football matters for this year as follows:

1. The starting date is set for the competition to begin on November 15th. 2. The competition system adopts a single round-robin competition method, with the team with the most points winning the championship. 3. The scoring method is that the winning team gets two points, the losing team gets zero points, and each team gets one point for a draw. If two teams are tied, a final will be held once, and the date will be determined by the committee. 4. The competition time starts at 3:00 PM, and the competition time is 90 minutes in total (45 minutes per half), with a one-minute rest. 5. The notary public is hired by the home team, but must obtain the consent of the visiting team. 6. The competition ball is shared by the home team using a new ball. 7. The competition rules are all implemented according to the Far Eastern Games football rules. 8. Rescheduling the competition If the venue cannot be used due to rain or other unavoidable circumstances, the rescheduling of the make-up game must be obtained from the other party. All procedures must be notified to the other party by the home team in advance. 9. Forfeiture If the team does not appear for the competition 15 minutes after the scheduled competition time, it will be considered a forfeiture, but players are not counted if they are delayed due to vehicle accidents on the way. 11. Reports Each winning team will send the results to various newspapers for publication on the same day after the competition and send a notice to the secretary's office within seven days at the latest. 12. List The names of all players in each team must be sent to the secretary for verification before November 14th.

Collection of Proposals from Various Parties

The Business and Industry Conference convened by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce is scheduled to open in Beijing on the 1st. Many members from Shanghai have been invited and are departing for Beijing today to attend. Listed below are the members who left for Beijing yesterday: Minister of Industry and Commerce Kong Xiangxi, Director Zhao Puqing, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce Lin Kanghou, Standing Committee members Chen Riping, Chairman of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Wang Xiaolai, Standing Committee members Wang Yansong, Ye Huijun, Executive Committee member Fang Jiaobo, Ye Fuxiao of the Continental Bank, Chen Zeqing, manager of the Four Banks Joint Treasury and president of Minghua Bank, Li Fusun, general manager of Zhejiang Industrial Bank, Zhang Gongquan, president of the Bank of China, Chen Guangfu, general manager of Shanghai Bank, Hu Mengjia, manager of the Bank of Communications, Huang Jinschen, chairman of the General Association of Silk Cocoon Producers of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, accountants Pan Xulun and Xu Yongzuo, President of Tongji University Hu Shuhua, Lao Jingxiu, director of Nanyang Tobacco Company, Zhang Zilian, general manager of Wangxing Cotton Mill, Yuan Duanfu, chairman of Ningbo Chamber of Commerce, Zheng Shouzhi, managing director of Jiangnan Paper Mill, Hu Bijiang, manager of Zhongnan Bank, Rong Zongjing, general manager of Shenxin Textile Mill, Wu Yunzhai, general manager of Jincheng Bank, Liu Hongsheng, general manager of China Cement Company, Zhu Mouxian, manager of Weicheng Company, Cai Shengbai, general manager of Meiya Silk Weaving Factory, Shao Jinqing, manager of Zhenhua Oil Paint Company, Lu Bohong, manager of China Electric Tram Company, Gu Xinyi of Huada Bank, Yang Xingfo, vice president of the Academia Sinica, and Wang Yiting, Wang Binyan, Qian Chengxu, Dai Ailu, Wu Yunshu, Ma Yinchu, Xiao Lizhai, Zhong Weicheng, Li Quanshi, Huang Zhangan, Liu Wanqing, Li Jinghan, Cai Zhengzhi, Yang Rumei, Shi Bo'an, Lu Chengzhang, Ren Sida, and others. The Shanghai Investigation Office of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce contacted the railway bureau yesterday to add dozens of sleeper berths to the evening train. It is said that the Industry and Commerce Conference will have people at the station to greet them upon arrival in Beijing. The proposals from various parties are listed below:

Pan Gongzhan: Representative of the Municipal Government and Director of the Bureau of Social Affairs, Pan Gongzhan, will report to Beijing today. The titles of the proposals he is submitting this time have been published in newspapers. It has been learned that the most important proposal is the "Motion for Unified Observance by All Industries of Regulations Approved by Competent Authorities" (Reason): It is found that if industry regulations formulated by industry associations and approved by competent authorities cannot be enforced on non-members, cunning individuals can arbitrarily expand their private interests, while members who join the association only have the obligation to bear the burdens without a common code of conduct, leading to regret and attempts to withdraw. This will make the association equivalent to a mere formality. (Measures): (1) The industry regulations formulated by each industry must be submitted to the local administrative authorities in charge of industry and commerce for approval and record. (2) Once approved and recorded, they will be regarded as industry regulations to be jointly observed. Whether a member or non-member, those who violate them may be reported to the authorities for investigation. (3) When the industry regulations encounter obstacles in practice, the authorities may add or delete them. There is also a "Motion to Promote Labor-Capital Cooperation" (Reason): Recently, all industries and businesses in Shanghai have suffered from the economic invasion of imperialists and the impact of labor-capital disputes, leading to successive bankruptcies. If no remedies are taken, the number of unemployed workers will inevitably increase. Our Party originally takes the protection of labor as one of its political programs. How can we sit idly by? Capital is apprehensive of the soaring costs and fearful of the surging labor unrest, making it impossible to maintain operations. If the skin is gone, what will the hair cling to? If we want to protect workers, we must first start with rescuing industries. (Measures): Each factory shall use profits to conduct labor welfare programs, and the government shall levy net profit taxes to allocate funds for local labor welfare programs. The measures are proposed as follows: (1) Stipulate minimum wages. (2) Stipulate the percentage of worker bonuses to encourage them. (3) Levy net profit taxes, stipulating progressive levels based on the amount, to conduct labor welfare programs and promote labor-capital cooperation. (4) Organize a local labor welfare program committee to preside over everything. Its members will be jointly appointed by Party and government agencies and representatives of both labor and capital. (5) Conduct labor welfare programs such as schools, hospitals, insurance, loans, dormitories, housing, pensions, unemployment insurance, unemployment subsidies, wage subsidies, etc. Other proposals include the "Motion to Encourage Private Basic Industries," "Motion to Rescue Key Industries such as Silk, Tea, Matches, Flour, Cigarettes, and Silk Weaving," and "Motion to Truly Use Domestic Goods." The reasons and measures for these proposals are lengthy and cannot be fully described. It is also heard that these proposals have been submitted to the Municipal Government for review and referral to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and will be submitted to the conference at that time.

Xu Peihuang: The newly appointed Director of the Education Bureau of this city, Xu Peihuang, has submitted several important proposals to the conference for inclusion on the agenda. The original text is very long. It has been learned that the content is as follows: (1) Request the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to announce to all industries and businesses nationwide to list and report in detail the problems in their respective industries, which the ministry will collect and study to separately resolve or improve, so that all industries and businesses have hope of recovery. (2) Limit foreign merchants from establishing factories in China to prevent foreign goods and semi-foreign goods from occupying the market and hindering the development of domestic factories. (3) Establish industrial and commercial management personnel training institutes to improve and enhance the intelligence of management personnel, and propose both short-term and long-term plans. (4) Request the establishment of industrial product standards in accordance with European and American methods, so that each manufacturer can specialize in their industry and avoid unnecessary waste.

Qian Chengxu: Qian Chengxu, a member of the Industry and Commerce Conference, proposed a "Motion to Request the Government to Promulgate Industrial Protection Laws as Soon as Possible to Benefit People's Livelihood and Emphasize Production." Under the current circumstances, China's industry is facing extreme difficulties. To realize the industrial policy laid down by the late Premier Sun Yat-sen, this conference can base on the legislative procedures promulgated by the Legislative Yuan to first discuss the scope. Once the principles are determined, the fundamental law of national industrial protection in the future can be generated accordingly, and all obstacles can be eliminated. In the late Premier Sun Yat-sen's "The International Development of China," private enterprises are stipulated to be encouraged by the state and laws are formulated to protect them. Eight principles are hereby proposed for discussion at the conference to determine whether they are appropriate for decision-making. (1) For all industries that have reached the level of foreign trade, the government should encourage their exports and exempt them from the burden of raw material taxes. (2) For foreign goods that have the nature of hoarding, the government should restrict their imports by law. (3) For Chinese and foreign merchants who operate industries and businesses in China with capital, the government should protect Chinese merchants or guarantee that they receive the same treatment as foreign merchants at a minimum. (4) For foreign manufacturers who operate industries and businesses in China, the government should order them to register with Chinese authorities. (5) For those who operate factories, the government should order local competent authorities to effectively protect the management rights of the factory in accordance with the law. (6) For those who operate financial institutions and whose business has developed to a certain extent, the government should order them to invest in certain industries. (7) For those who operate factories, the government may order them to rectify and improve all their internal operations and equipment to conform to the principles of scientific management. (8) For those who operate factories with capital and whose products are no longer needed in the market, or who deliberately lower prices in the market to compete, and whose purpose is to monopolize the future market, the government should adopt intervention policies.

Machine-Made Goods Association: The Shanghai Machine-Made National Goods Factory Association sent a telegram to the Industry and Commerce Conference: "To the Secretariat of the Nanjing Industry and Commerce Conference, for the public review of all members: This Industry and Commerce Conference is aimed at promoting benefits and eliminating ills, covering all aspects. The reason why our national goods cannot develop is that the tax rates on national goods and foreign goods are not equal. Taking the national cotton cloth, which is a daily necessity for the people, as an example, each bolt of national cloth pays 1.333 taels of tax (likin excluded), while each bolt of foreign cloth pays 0.21 taels of tax. For national cloth of the same weight (less than 10 taels), each bolt pays 1.122 taels more tax than foreign goods. At a time when the government is advocating national goods, national goods are obviously being ostracized by foreign goods, making it difficult to develop. What should be done to remedy this? Please pay special attention to this matter. Shanghai Machine-Made National Goods Factory Association."

The Municipal Government issued an instruction to the Bureau of Social Affairs yesterday: "In order to implement the order, we have received the Executive Yuan's instruction No. 3711, which states that in accordance with the Nanjing Municipal Government's request to reiterate the ban on strict prohibition of rice exports to maintain the people's food supply, we have submitted the situation to the National Government for review and implementation.
