Issues Concerning Industry Regulations 126

The Bureau of Social Affairs Requested Further Review on the Issue of Whether Industry Regulations Should Be Observed. The matter has recently attracted considerable attention. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce recently made a submission to the Bureau of Social Affairs, which the Bureau has forwarded to the Municipal Government. The submission reads as follows: "Submission Regarding the Request for Instructions. We have received Your Honor's Instruction No. 5624 (omitted in the middle). We have ordered the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to notify them. The Chamber of Commerce has submitted that if the competent authorities are responsible for handling industrial and commercial matters within their jurisdiction, it is their exclusive responsibility. If the industry regulations requested for filing by each industry contain provisions that are deemed to involve monopolies or violate good customs, it would be difficult to lightly approve them. Historically, cases of rejection can be investigated. The Ministry's order states that even if they are filed, it is still difficult to guarantee that there will be no malpractices. It seems unlikely that the authorities would handle matters so lightly. It also states that such bad regulations are difficult to protect even if they are brought to court. If this statement is followed, even if the members who have joined the association seek relief by appealing to the law because they do not comply with the regulations agreed upon by the public, they will lose their protection. We are afraid that once this order is disseminated, all regulations will not only be insufficient to bind non-members, but also insufficient to bind members who have joined the association. From then on, the association will no longer have any binding force. How can we expect it to seek public interest for the industry? Furthermore, the state's permission to establish industry associations clearly recognizes them as maintaining public interests and correcting business malpractices. Now, the regulations submitted by each association for approval are denounced as 'often containing monopolistic nature or violating good customs.' It is as if the establishment of the association is no different from creating a mechanism for industry monopoly. If what is said is true, wouldn't the merchants have cases of accusation and the authorities have grounds for dissolution? We believe that what the Ministry emphasizes is nothing more than that the regulations do not conform to good customs and the authorities have not been able to examine them in detail. Therefore, even if they are filed, it is still difficult to guarantee that there will be no malpractices. This should have been clearly stated by the competent authorities without the need for the association to elaborate. However, since the Ministry's order states that the competent authorities should still refer to good commercial customs to carefully review the regulations established by each industry in order to reduce disputes, and also states that regardless of the content of the regulations, those approved by the authorities, whether or not they have joined the association, must comply. Not only will it not help, but it will also cause disputes. If the content of the regulations does not violate good commercial customs, and has been solemnly decided by the industry in advance and carefully approved by the authorities, the situation is no different from being a recognized business practice in the industry. If the scope of implementation is limited to members who have joined the association, those who have not joined will take advantage of their private interests, and those who have joined will withdraw one after another. The various associations will either be in the form of disintegration or will exist in name only and lose their effectiveness. This is a detailed study of the business situation and the experience gained, and it is not empty talk. Business customs of an industry are within the scope of not conflicting with commercial laws and regulations, and there is a supplementary legal effect. The regulations decided and filed are actually the written commercial customs. In terms of the general rule of supplementing laws and regulations with customs, it cannot be said that there is no mandatory effect. It is a matter of fact that it is necessary to order non-members to comply with the regulations, and it is not without basis in law. It is appropriate to prepare a document and request for review. We respectfully request your decision. Respectfully submitted to Mayor Zhang."

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Submitted a Request to Maintain the Municipal Chamber of Commerce's Request That Non-Member Industries Should Comply With the Regulations, and Resubmitted the Request to the Bureau of Social Affairs. "Submission Regarding the Fact That the Regulations Are Important to Each Industry Association, and the Public Lost Their Minds After Receiving the Ministry's Rejection. They Gathered to Discuss and Request for Maintenance, and Submitted the Situation to Request Your Honor to Review and Approve. We Request the Municipal Government to Resubmit to the Executive Yuan to Order the Ministry to Re-Examine the Matters. On the 29th of this month, we received a joint letter from the Southern Goods Industry, Intestine Industry, Egg Industry, Silk Industry, Northern and Southern Goods Exchange Industry, Fruit and Local Goods Industry, Soy Sauce Garden Industry, Chinese Medicine Industry, Medicinal Material Industry, Chinese Woolen Factory Industry, Transportation Industry, Chinese Soap Industry, Chicken and Duck Industry, and the Eighty-Fourth Industry Association, requesting the Association to Submit Approved Regulations for Re-Examination so That They Can Be Followed, etc. (The original text is omitted). It was found that this case was first submitted by Your Bureau to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to the Executive Yuan. It is believed that in this case, the Ministry failed to thoroughly understand the commercial situation. Once implemented, it is feared that each association will inevitably disintegrate as a result. We have explained the reasons in detail and requested to resubmit to the Executive Yuan for the Ministry to re-examine. The approval for review has been received. However, no clear text has been seen to be submitted to the Ministry for re-examination for many days. This time, each industry association appointed tax coupon recognition, which is based on the fact that non-member industries are not bound by the association and cannot recognize it. The member industries also found it extremely difficult to handle the situation because the obligations were too skewed. They repeatedly asked the association for instructions and refused to handle the matter. All of these situations show that the division between member and non-member industries makes it difficult to handle the various facts. The only way to remedy this is to allow the regulations to be complied with uniformly, so that it can be maintained to a slight extent. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce is in charge of the whole country and cannot deeply understand the hardships. This time, each association has come to us with letters stating that their reasons are in line with the previous submissions of the affiliated associations. Since the associations have entrusted their intentions, it is not appropriate to suppress them. We will prepare a document stating the situation and requesting Your Bureau to review and forward it. It is truly a convenience for the public."

The Second Meeting of the Regulations Protection Committee: The Industry Association Regulations Protection Committee of this city held its second committee meeting yesterday. Chairman Luo Qinghua resolved the following motions: (1) A letter from the Hat Association requesting the authorities to amend the motion that all industries in a region must join the industry association was discussed and a reply was sent. (2) A motion to have the committee members hold a face-to-face meeting with Chairman Jiang when he passes through Shanghai to appeal for the maintenance of the regulations was approved. (3) A motion to submit a request to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to allow the committee to send members to participate in the Industry and Commerce Conference so that they can raise the issue of regulations was discussed and a telegram was sent to the chairman of the Industry and Commerce Conference and Mr. Wang Yansong was requested to urge the representatives to strive for this. (4) A motion to send representatives to the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee and the National Government to petition for protection was approved. The meeting was adjourned after the discussions.

Important Remarks by Wang Yansong: The various industry associations in this city believe that the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's discussion and rejection of the regulations is a major issue and will inevitably render the various industry associations merely formal. They convened a joint meeting of representatives of various industries some days ago and resolved to organize an Industry Association Regulations Protection Committee to handle the matter exclusively. Yesterday, the committee held its second committee meeting to discuss the direction of progress. After the meeting, it was learned that the Bureau of Social Affairs of this city had submitted a proposal to the Industry and Commerce Conference on the issue. It was also learned that Mr. Wang Yansong, a standing committee member of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and a member of the Industry and Commerce Conference, was very concerned about the situation of the various industries. He then organized a team to meet with Mr. Wang Yansong to request assistance. Mr. Wang Yansong met with the committee members of the association and stated that the use of regulations is to correct business malpractices and promote public interests. Unfavorable habits such as shoddy workmanship and materials, counterfeit goods, and disturbing market prices are all eliminated by the constraints of regulations, and the morality and credit of commerce can also be mutually improved. However, such regulations must be observed by both member and non-member industries to be effective. Otherwise, those who join the association must fulfill all social obligations and be bound by the regulations. Why not allow those who have not joined the association to be free and do whatever they want? Therefore, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce is also very concerned about this. After the Ministry of Industry and Commerce discussed and rejected the regulations, it explained the reasons and requested a review. Now that the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs has submitted a proposal to the Industry and Commerce Conference, I, as a member of the conference, will certainly strive for it at that time. Fortunately, the gentlemen who are discussing the issue at the Industry and Commerce Conference are all from the business community and have a wealth of experience. I believe they will have extremely perfect opinions to contribute to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for adoption. After saying this, the committee members left with excitement.

Investigation of Countries With and Without Treaties 129

The Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau issued a notice yesterday stating that in order to facilitate the handling of cases involving foreign nationals in the city, the Bureau had previously sent a letter to the Europe and America Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to request a detailed reply on the names of countries with consular jurisdiction, the names of countries with treaties, the names of countries without treaties, and the names of countries that have signed treaties but have not yet been implemented. Now, we have received a reply with an enclosed list of countries with and without treaties. We are hereby notifying the district directors. This order includes a list of countries with and without treaties: "Names of Countries With Treaties": (1) Countries that have treaty relations and are completely subject to Chinese jurisdiction: Russia, Germany, Austria, Finland, Persia, Greece, Mexico, Bolivia, Chile. (2) Countries that have accepted Chinese jurisdiction but must wait until more than half of the countries with consular jurisdiction have waived their rights before implementation: Belgium. (3) Countries that have accepted Chinese jurisdiction but must wait until the countries that signed the Washington Conference agree before implementation: Italy, Spain, Portugal, Denmark. (4) The old treaties have not yet expired, and our country has declared that it will recover jurisdiction from January 19th, but will temporarily handle matters as they were before the implementation measures have not been determined: England, America, France, Holland, Norway, Brazil. (5) The old treaties have expired, and new treaties have not yet been signed. In fact, they will be temporarily handled as they were: Japan, Sweden, Peru. The original treaties stipulate that countries that abolish consular jurisdiction will also be allowed to do so: Switzerland. "Names of Countries Without Treaties": (1) All countries except those with treaties mentioned in the previous article are countries without treaties. (2) Even if they have sent envoys and consuls, but have not yet signed commercial treaties, they can still be regarded as countries without treaties: Cuba, Panama, Nicaragua. "Names of Countries That Have Signed Treaties But Have Not Yet Been Implemented": (1) Czech Republic (2) Poland. Before implementation, they are still regarded as countries without treaties.

Change of Command for the French New and Old Asian Squadrons 130

The newly appointed Vice Admiral Hall Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday Afternoon

Installation Ceremony Scheduled for the 5th of Next Month on the Flagship

Outgoing Rear Admiral Maugue Departs Shanghai on the 8th

The newly appointed French Asian Fleet Commander, Vice Admiral Hall, arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon aboard the French postal ship "Asia Third Voyage." French Consul General Kang-ge-lin and outgoing Commander Rear Admiral Maugue, among others, greeted him at the dock. Vice Admiral Hall is temporarily residing at the Cathay Hotel. He is scheduled to assume command on the flagship "Jean-Jacques Rousseau" on the 5th of next month. The French authorities plan to host a banquet on the evening of the 4th at the French Club to welcome the Vice Admiral and introduce him to Chinese and foreign officials and businessmen. Vice Admiral Hall joined the navy at the age of seventeen and has served for forty years, holding various important positions. This time, he was transferred from the Chairman of the Naval Technical Committee and Chairman of the New Ship Trial Committee to the Fleet Commander. Accompanying him are fifteen people, including the ship's captain and adjutant. Outgoing Commander Rear Admiral Maugue and the retiring naval personnel will depart Shanghai on the 8th of next month aboard the French postal ship "La Ville de la Ciotat". Yesterday, the French Concession Municipal Council specially prepared a gold medal, which was presented by French Consul General Kang-ge-lin to Rear Admiral Maugue as a memento.

Meiya Silk Factory Fashion Exhibition 131

Grand Occasion Held at the Great China Hotel Yesterday

Mayor Zhang and Others Attended to Deliver Speeches

The Meiya Silk Weaving Factory, founded entirely by Chinese people, was established in the ninth year of the Republic of China. This year marks its tenth anniversary. Its products are of excellent quality and its business is thriving. General Manager Mr. Cai Sheng-bai has planned effectively, resulting in continuous improvement of the organization and increasing product innovation. It now has fourteen branch factories, supplying goods to Europe, America, Southeast Asia, India, and China. It is truly a pioneer of domestic silk factories. Yesterday afternoon at 4 p.m., the Tenth Anniversary Fashion Exhibition was held at the Great China Hotel. The atmosphere was filled with the fragrance of clothing and hair ornaments, and the rustling of skirts and shoes. The event was extremely grand. Approximately 2,000 guests attended from all sectors, including political, military, business, academic circles, and prominent ladies. Shanghai Mayor Zhang Yuejun stayed from the beginning of the opening ceremony until the end of the event, and personally delivered a speech. The grand occasion of yesterday is recorded in detail below:

Attending Guests: Shanghai Mayor Zhang Yuejun and his wife, Municipal Government Secretary-General Yu Hongjun and his wife, Director of the Social Affairs Bureau Pan Gongzhan and his wife, Representative of Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce Zhao Jinqing, Shanghai Municipal Party Committee Member Fan Zhengbo and his wife, Minister of Foreign Affairs Wang Zhengting and his wife, Director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs Shanghai Office Liu Yunfang and his wife, President of the Jiangsu Higher Second Court Xu Weizhen and his wife, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce members, owner of the Jinda New Silk Fabric Bureau Wang Yansong and his wife, as well as various bureau chiefs of the Municipal Government and prominent ladies Guo Anzi, Yu Xiuyun, and others; movie stars Hu Die, Yan Yuexian, and others. In total, there were over 2,000 guests from all sectors. There was no empty seat in the venue, and those who arrived late to purchase tickets were unable to enter due to the lack of space, with about 700 people being forced to turn back.

Venue Decoration: All decorations in the venue were undertaken by the Meiyi Architectural Firm, based on designs by a French-educated artist, Mr. [Blank Space]. The decorations were all very modern in style. At the entrance, there was a colorful archway, and more than forty brocade screens were displayed, all showcasing the factory's printed and plain-colored high-quality silks in very delicate colors. In the center of the dance hall, a round platform was built, with a pond in the center from which a large silk umbrella lamp emerged. To the right of the round platform, a long bridge led to the entrance for the fashion show performers. All around were seats for the guests. During the opening ceremony, speeches, reports, and music were broadcast throughout the venue using extremely large Telefunken speakers installed by Siemens, ensuring orderly proceedings and excellent results.

Opening Ceremony: The ceremony began at approximately 4 p.m. After singing the national anthem and performing customary salutations, General Manager Cai of the factory delivered the opening speech. This was followed by speeches from Mayor Zhang, Director Zhao representing Minister Kong of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, Director Pan of the Social Affairs Bureau, and others. The fashion show then began, interspersed with tea dances and entertainment. Finally, a film produced by the factory itself, titled "Chinese Silk," was screened. It described the earliest invention of Chinese silk weaving and lamented the lack of improvement due to adherence to old methods, which prevented it from competing with Europe and America. It depicted the ancient and modern methods of silkworm farming, silk reeling, and silk weaving, as well as the operations of the Meiya factory. The music began to play as the film ended, and the meeting adjourned at 7:30 p.m.

Opening Speech: General Manager Cai's opening speech stated, in brief: "Today, we celebrate the tenth anniversary of our factory and invite guests from all walks of life to attend and provide guidance. We are deeply honored and grateful. When our factory was founded ten years ago, our capital was limited and our scale was small. However, with the guidance of various sectors and the enthusiastic promotion of domestic products, we have been able to gradually develop. The purpose of today's fashion exhibition is not to boast about our products, but to earnestly seek guidance from all sectors. We hope you will forgive any inadequacies or discourtesies in today's reception."

Mayor's Speech: Shanghai Mayor Zhang Yuejun delivered a speech stating, in brief: "Promoting domestic products requires attention to four aspects: 1. The quantity of domestic products; 2. The quality of domestic products; 3. The compatibility of domestic products with national conditions; 4. The business ethics of domestic products. The products of Meiya Factory are large in quantity, excellent in quality, suitable for national conditions, and beneficial to national productivity. Furthermore, they pay great attention to business ethics. Their future is immeasurable. I am very pleased to participate in this event and wish Meiya Factory to be a vital force in the domestic products industry, with even greater development in the future."

Photograph of the Meiya Fashion Exhibition (Taken by Zhonghua Photography Studio)

Mr. Zhao's Speech: Zhao Jinqing, Director of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, delivered a speech stating, in brief: "Today, Minister Kong has entrusted me to deliver a speech on his behalf. I feel that in these times of poverty and financial difficulty, everyone lacks food because industry and commerce are declining and production is too weak. Even in the silk industry, the situation is not as good as it used to be. However, today's event can give us a lesson: Meiya Factory has achieved this good result through ten years of effort. If all domestic products could be like this, then the development of national industry and commerce could be achieved quickly, and the hardship of the people's livelihood could be alleviated. I hope that Meiya Silk Factory will continue to make progress and be a model for the effort of domestic industrial and commercial enterprises."

Mr. Pan's Speech: Director Pan Gongzhan of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau delivered a speech stating, in brief: "Promoting domestic products is no longer a time for talk but a time for action. To promote domestic products, the people only need to fulfill their responsibilities and purchase domestic products as much as possible within their capabilities, and domestic products will naturally develop. The history of Meiya Factory is only ten years, but its efforts have achieved remarkable results in production. Therefore, consumption must also be the same. I believe that with our large population, we can become rich and strong simply by being self-sufficient, and there is no need to make the export of domestic products a major benefit. However, the decline of the silk industry abroad may not be a bad phenomenon. If our people can work hard to promote domestic silk products, and the raw materials are from ourselves and used by ourselves, why worry about the lack of sales? Therefore, the future of Meiya Factory is very promising. After another ten years, its development will be even greater than it is now."

Fashion Show: The fashion show featured a total of twenty-four outfits modeled by several Chinese and Western ladies. They emerged from the dressing room, walked slowly and gracefully across the long bridge, and stepped onto the round platform. They turned around once to the accompaniment of beautiful music, and then retreated gracefully. The scene was particularly charming and eye-catching under the red lights, and the overall effect was magnificent. The show was divided into three acts. The first act was dedicated to morning wear: 1. Sleepwear; 2. Underwear; 3. Lounge wear. The second act was dedicated to general daytime wear: 1. Garden party wear; 2. Outerwear; 3. Tennis wear; 4. Tea dance wear. The third act was dedicated to evening wear: 1. Evening dress; 2. Evening gown.

Inauguration Ceremony of Chen Qimei Memorial Tower Scheduled 132

The Chen Qimei Memorial Tower, built at the Fangbang Bridge in the West Gate of this city, has been under construction for almost six months. The entire tower project has now been completed, and the inauguration ceremony is scheduled for the 3rd of next month. The tower preparation office has also sent invitations to various military and political institutions in this city to attend the ceremony and has built a guest platform surrounded by bamboo fences for rest. The tower is eighty feet high and contains an iron ladder leading to the top. The front faces east, and the following inscription is engraved in large seal script on the marble base: "Memorial Tower of Mr. Chen Qimei." A door in the back wall provides access. On both sides are engraved the "Memorial Tower Inscription of Mr. Chen Qimei." A round vessel tops the tower, rising majestically into the clouds, creating a solemn atmosphere. The inscription is recorded below:

(Memorial Tower Inscription of Mr. Chen Qimei) Mr. Chen's given name was Qimei, a native of Wuxing, Zhejiang. During the recovery of Shanghai in the Xinhai Revolution, he was elected as the Shanghai Governor. He met with the armies of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Guangdong, and Guangxi to capture Nanjing, welcomed the Prime Minister at sea, and established the Republic of China. When Hongxian declared himself emperor, he planned to rise up in the southeast to restore the Republic. On May 18th of the fifth year, he was assassinated in Shanghai at the age of thirty-nine. His wife, Yao, and orphan, Zu Zuhe, waited until it had been fourteen years since Mr. Chen's death when his old friends Huang Fu of Hangzhou, Jiang Zhongzheng of Fenghua, and Zhang Qun of Huayang were finally able to fulfill the wishes of the people of Shanghai and requested land to erect a tower for Mr. Chen. Alas, Mr. Chen's painstaking efforts in the early stages of the revolution, his selfless courage in the face of difficulties, and his dedication to the cause until its success are all recorded in the national history and should be as long-lasting as the Republic of China, enduring for all time and never being replaced. This cannot be fully recorded by a mere corner of land or a single stone. Only the people of Shanghai cannot remain silent. Recalling that nineteen years ago, Shanghai, a small place, was tied to the success or failure of each province, and Mr. Chen, as an individual, determined the safety of Shanghai. Transportation converged here, finances were provided, military affairs were prepared, and public opinion was gathered. On the night of November 3rd of the Xinhai year, the people's army attacked the Shanghai Southern Manufacturing Bureau without success. Mr. Chen said, "I will use righteousness to inform them so that they will surrender without fighting and avoid harming their compatriots and alarming the people." He rushed in alone, and although he was captured, he eloquently spoke of the necessity of reforming the government and the urgency of the revolution. When the city was captured, Mr. Chen, with his hands in iron chains, came out and said, "Aren't the comrades suffering enough?" His demeanor was solemn. Alas, is this not what is meant by forgetting oneself in the face of danger and not yielding when faced with righteousness? In governing the army, Mr. Chen shared the joys and hardships with his soldiers. In governing the government, he advocated thrift to cultivate integrity. In his residence, the house had only two pillars, and all the instruments in the Governor's mansion were simple. Mr. Chen said, "The disease of a weak country is deep-rooted. If we want to revitalize the spirit of the people, we must rectify the declining customs. Shanghai is a bustling area where the rich and poor are vastly different. Using military force is only a last resort to remove the old and bring in the new. How can we bear to see this brief moment become the final path to light? Why suddenly indulge in trivial matters and open up endless evil examples?" Alas, Mr. Chen can be said to have possessed the virtues of benevolence, courage, integrity, and modesty. Mr. Chen pioneered the Shanghai city, initiated the demolition of the city walls, and today the towering thoroughfares and densely packed residences were created by Mr. Chen. Now, a tower is erected to promote his achievements and to ride on immortality. Is this not appropriate? The foundation of the tower was laid on May 18th of the 19th year of the Republic of China, marking the day of Mr. Chen's death. It was completed on November 3rd of the same year, not forgetting Mr. Chen's contribution to the recovery of Shanghai. The funds were donated by private individuals, following Mr. Chen's intention of cherishing public funds. So that those who view it in the future may have a place to admire and admire. It is tied with a song, saying: "Alas, Mr. Chen's life was filled with worries and toil; Mr. Chen's death made his name immortal. Knowing that his heroic spirit loves this land, may his soul forever encircle the city of Shanghai. May the country of China be glorious and prosperous, and may the people of China be peaceful and happy. May this comfort his spirit, which will never perish in heaven and earth."

Ministry of Railways Tightens Control of Railway Funds 135

Circular Issued to Two Railway Bureaus for Compliance

Minister of Railways Sun Ke recently stated that although the income from passenger and freight transport on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway this year has increased significantly compared to last year, the rising gold price has affected the payment of interest on loans from silver companies. The principal and interest due for the first half of the year have not yet been repaid, and the principal and interest due for the second half of the year are about to be due. Therefore, a circular was issued to the two railway bureaus requiring them to tighten their belts and reduce expenditures except for urgent matters that need to be undertaken, in order to benefit the finances and supplement the remedy.

Yuan Shunwu Escapes After Being Kidnapped: Details of the Ordeal 138

Xiao Jianxing's Sister Learns to Dance at Fang's

Fang Dewen Claims He Has a Generous Reward

Liu Changming Kneels Before His Elderly Mother

Another Suspect Arrested Yesterday

Five days after being kidnapped, Yuan Shunwu, a second-year student at Datong University on Zhongshan Road in West Shanghai, was rescued by the Sixth District police, who captured the main culprits. The details of the kidnapping and rescue have already been reported in this newspaper. After learning the details of the successful rescue in this case, which was quite interesting, we are providing a more detailed account below:

After Yuan was kidnapped, District Chief Ren of the Sixth District received the report and personally led Inspector Xu and the entire team of detectives to pursue the kidnappers, but without success. District Chief Ren then inquired with the Shi surname student who witnessed Yuan's kidnapping about all the details. Shi stated that Zou Yaodong, who currently resides at 123 Hanbi Li Road in Hongkou, was well acquainted with Yuan. When Yuan was kidnapped, three bandits claimed that Zou had come to visit Yuan, and Yuan, unsuspecting, went out. The three bandits then forced Yuan into a car, so Zou was highly suspected. On the morning of the 25th, Inspector Xu was ordered to go to Zou's residence in Hongkou with Detective Team Leader Liu Shaoqing, detectives Gan Youxin, Hu Rui, Wang Zengfa, and Tang Bingxiang, and arrest Zou. Zou was transferred to the Special District Court. Inspector Xu requested extradition, which was approved, and Zou was taken back to the station. District Chief Ren repeatedly interrogated Zou, who claimed to be well acquainted with Yuan and firmly denied any involvement in the case. Late that evening, Zou suggested that Xiao Jianxing, who resides at 112 Fuchunfang, Fangbang Road, must be involved. On the morning of the 26th, District Chief Ren sent Liu Shaoqing and Gan Youxin to Xiao's residence, but Xiao and his wife had already left early in the morning, according to the second landlord. However, Yang, who teaches Xiao's sister to dance, was at home. Liu inquired with Yang, who claimed not to know where Xiao had gone. Xiao's wife, Yu, was currently at 105 East Yalu Road in Hongkou. Liu instructed Yang to lead the way and ordered Wang Zengfa, Tang Bingxiang, and Hu Rui to guard Xiao's residence. Liu and others went to Yu's residence and arrested her, taking her back to the station. District Chief Ren interrogated Yu, who claimed to be nineteen years old. She did not know whether her husband was involved in Yuan Shunwu's kidnapping, but she did know that Yi Peihan, who resided on the third floor of a clothing store at 31 Ximenli, Ximen Road, was the mastermind. She also did not know where her husband had gone. District Chief Ren then sent Liu Shaoqing and others to Ximenli to arrest Yi, but without success. Just as they returned to the station, Wang Zengfa and others had guarded and arrested Xiao Jianxing, bringing him to the station. District Chief Ren interrogated Xiao, who claimed to be twenty-eight years old and from Hanyang. Initially, he firmly denied any involvement in Yuan's case. Only after his wife was brought in for questioning did he confess that Yi Peihan was the mastermind, but Yi had already taken residence in a hotel across from the Qingquan Bathhouse in the concession, and his name had been changed to Ye Kang. He was scheduled to go to Hanyang the next day. After obtaining this information, District Chief Ren ordered the five detectives Liu Shaoqing and Gan Youxin to go to various hotels at the border between the British and French concessions to investigate. Before long, Wang Zengfa and Tang Bingxiang found Ye Kang in Room 30 of the Unified Hotel. They immediately joined Liu and others and entered the room. The bellhop said that the guest had gone out and would not return until 12:00. Liu and others then opened a room in Room 36 and waited inside. Around 11:00, a person came to Room 30 and knocked on the door, calling for Ye. Liu and others immediately lured the person back to their room. The person, who was identified as Fang Dewen, knew he had been caught by detectives and immediately handed over 170 yuan to Gan, begging for help. Gan sealed the money in red paper and had it inspected by the French Concession detective. Liu and others waited until 1:30 and not seeing Ye, took Fang to the French Concession police station. The police chief briefly interrogated Fang and confirmed that Liu and others were allowed to take him back. As they were getting into the car, Fang again promised Liu and Gan to reward them with 500 yuan the next day, asking for their help. After taking him to the station, District Chief Ren received a phone call from the Public Security Bureau saying that Yi Peihan had been arrested by a supervisor on the ship. District Chief Ren immediately escorted the Fang to the Public Security Bureau. On the 27th, the Third Section Chief of the Public Security Bureau interrogated Yi and Fang and concluded that the kidnapping had been orchestrated by Liu Changming, an Anhui native living in the fourth house in Huaxingfang. All they needed to do was interrogate Liu. District Chief Ren waited until 2:00 a.m. on the 28th and personally led the entire team of detectives and two patrol officers Xu and Wei to the address. They arrested Liu Changming and took him to the First Division of the Fourth District. Liu then readily confessed, but said that since he had committed the crime and was arrested, he deserved to be punished. He would surely be shot in the future. He only begged the District Chief to let him see his seventy-year-old mother. District Chief Ren sent a police officer to bring his mother over. Liu knelt down and said to his mother, "I have committed such a crime and cannot repay my mother's kindness in raising me. I deserve to die and will only be able to repay you in the next life." He also asked the District Chief to fulfill his request. District Chief Ren, seeing his pitiful old mother, sent a police officer to take her home. As the mother left, Liu said that he would go and find the hostage. Liu then led the way to rescue the hostage Yuan. This is the beginning and the end of the entire ordeal. Also, the Sixth District Public Security Bureau learned that a kidnapper named Wang Leshan from Anhui was looking for someone at that address. Yao, the Chief of the First Division of the Fourth District, learned of this and immediately led two patrol officers Ye and Li and armed police to Ninganfang to arrest Wang. They found 53 yuan in cash on his person and learned that he had a check for 200 yuan stored in a hotel. Chief Yao Benyuan verified the confession and concluded that Wang Leshan was carrying cash and had a check deposited in the hotel, which was related to the bandits, and ordered him to be taken to the bureau for investigation.

The Stoker Only Returns Home Every Six Months

So the Wife Has an Affair

Wu Aifeng, a 23-year-old woman from Ningbo, used to be a hostess at the rooftop garden of the New World Company. On September 21st of last year, she married Weng Shude, a fellow villager, and they lived together at 1547 Seward Road. Weng worked as a stoker in the engine room of a German foreign ship. The ship traveled between Germany and Shanghai, so Weng could only return home once every six months. Wu Aifeng, because her husband was away from home for a long time, was unaccustomed to sleeping alone and had an affair. Some time ago, the ship arrived in Shanghai from abroad, and Weng returned home. Wu immediately told Weng that there was no money for household expenses and it was difficult to make ends meet. Weng then gave her 235 yuan. Wu took the money and ran away without a trace. Weng became suspicious and investigated carefully, and learned that his wife had been having an affair with a butcher named Zhou Heshang and had rented a house at 953 Datong Road, Shanhai Pass Road, acting like a married couple. No. 2194 in the nearby chinese settlement heard the alarm and rushed to apprehend Wu Aifeng, Zhou Heshang, and Weng Shude together to the Xinzha Police Station. When asked to the defendant Wu Aifeng, the defendant Wu Aifeng confessed that the plaintiff used to live not far from my house in Tongzhou Road, and I often went out to drink water, and the plaintiff came to flirt with me, so I had an affair. At that time, my mother was ill and learned of this matter and was furious and wanted to beat me to death, so I went directly to the plaintiff's place on September 21st of last year to live together. I and the plaintiff are also having an affair and not a formal couple, but I admit to having an affair with Zhou Heshang. This time, the plaintiff came home from abroad and confined me at home for several days. Then, on a certain day, two of the plaintiff's friends came to discuss with the plaintiff about wanting to take me to a foreign port to sell me. I heard this and was terrified, so I took the opportunity to escape under the pretext of buying alcohol. When questioned, Zhou Heshang said that in March of this year, I went to the New World Company to play, and Wu came to serve tea. After talking to each other, Wu said that her husband was working abroad and there was no money at home, so she asked me to help. I then invited friends to Wu's house to play mahjong and became acquainted and had an affair. I first rented a house on the upper floor of the Yitaixiang tobacco and paper shop on Yunnan Road, and moved to Datong Road at the beginning of this month, etc. After verifying the confession, Judge Cheng ordered the two defendants to each pay 500 yuan in guarantee money and wait for a rescheduled hearing.

Extension of Technician Certificate Renewal Period 144

A Final Extension of Six Months

The Municipal Government Notified the Public Works Bureau Yesterday

According to Articles 13 and 14 of the Regulations for the Implementation of Technician Registration, individuals who obtained certificates according to the separate regulations for technician registration by local governments before the implementation of the Technician Registration Regulations, and those who passed the technician qualification examination of the former Beijing Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce, should apply to the competent ministry for certificate issuance within six months of the new regulations' implementation. The effective date of these regulations was October 10, 1929. Therefore, the issuance of registration certificates for the technicians mentioned in the aforementioned two articles should have ceased after April 10, 1930. However, the Ministries of Industry, Commerce, Agriculture, and Mining found that the number of applicants complying with the regulations and applying for certificate issuance by the deadline was still limited. Considering that people in remote provinces and regions were unable to apply for new certificates on time due to transportation difficulties, they submitted a request to extend the deadline by another six months. Nevertheless, by October 10, 1930, the deadline expired again. The two ministries reviewed the qualified technician examination files transferred from the former Beijing Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce, and found that many had still not applied for new certificates according to the law. Although there were no quotas or verifiable files for technicians registered with local governments, the number of those who had been granted extensions was still very small. It was found that the main reason was that the internal political situation in the country, the suppression of the reactionary military, had not been fully completed, and that bandit-communist disturbances made travel unsafe, making it impossible to renew certificates by the deadline. To show leniency, the two ministries submitted another request for a further extension of six months, declaring that there would be no further extensions after the deadline to emphasize the limitations. It is learned that the Shanghai Municipal Government received instructions from the Executive Yuan yesterday regarding the extension of the technician certificate renewal deadline and immediately instructed the Public Works Bureau to notify the public.

Shipping Accident During Storm 147

Wheat Vessel Capsizes, Crew Missing

Great Losses Due to Soaked Wheat

Ship owner Yang Maomao recently loaded 200 dan of wheat in Pingwang and set sail for Shanghai to deliver it to a certain flour mill. The ship arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday and docked south of the Nanshi Cement Factory. Because it was not unloaded, Yang and others returned home, leaving only a crew member and an apprentice to guard the ship. However, around 2:00 AM yesterday morning, it rained heavily, coinciding with high tide. The guards were asleep when the rain became heavy, the load increased, and the mooring rope was broken by the waves. The ship capsized. The guards and the apprentice woke up in panic, both falling into the river. However, the apprentice grabbed the mooring rope and pulled himself up. The other crew member is missing. Fortunately, the ship was in a shallow area and was leaning against the riverbank. However, the wheat in the front cabin was lost, and half of the wheat in the middle cabin was also lost. The remaining wheat was soaked in water. When Yang and others arrived at the ship yesterday morning to unload the cargo, they saw that the ship had capsized. They immediately hired a boat to help upright the ship. After inspecting the ship, they found that most of the oars and equipment were lost. Only sixty or seventy dan of wheat remained, and the bow of the ship was damaged. They immediately reported to the flour mill and requested that they hire a boat to unload the wheat. However, upon learning this, the factory sent someone to inspect the ship and saw that the goods inside the ship were already wet, so they refused to accept the wheat. The estimated losses are huge. They immediately telegraphed the wheat merchant in Pingwang to inform them of the loss. It is unknown who will bear this loss.

Charcoal Baskets Filled with Opium 149

Totaling 105 Taels

Chen Er'a Detained for One Year

The day before yesterday at noon, a cart puller named Chen Moji from Tongzhou was transporting seven baskets of charcoal through Qichang Road. Chinese Constable No. 1847 and Western Detective Xiang No. 372 from the Hongkou Police Station found his behavior suspicious and questioned him. Chen stated that the cart was going to the New Dahua Hotel at No. 147 Fuzhou Road to deliver the charcoal. The detective then ordered the constable to follow behind while he went to wait in front of the hotel. After a while, Chen Er'a from Wuxi came out to receive the goods. Seeing the detectives and constables nearby, he realized the situation was dire and turned around to run into the hotel, closing the door. The detectives and constables broke down the door, arrested Chen, and the cart puller Chen Moji pointed out that Chen Er'a was his employer. The detectives and constables then opened the charcoal baskets and found 105 taels of opium hidden at the bottom. They were all taken to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the Special District Local Court. Lawyer Zhang Tianyin of the police station stated the case and claimed that the cart puller Chen Moji was a witness but was detained for questioning due to concerns about his potential involvement. Chen Er'a claimed that someone surnamed Jia, who was on the run, had shipped the charcoal baskets from the Yangtze River to Shanghai and unloaded them at the Ewo Wharf. He only asked Chen Moji to transport the seven baskets of charcoal to the hotel because he temporarily had a loose tongue. He claimed he was waiting there and did not know that the charcoal contained opium. His remaining testimony was evasive. Chen Moji stated that Chen Er'a asked him to send the seven baskets of charcoal to the hotel at the wharf, and he knew nothing else. He also stated that he had not received the six jiao cart fee and asked for judgment. Judge Ge Zhitian verified that Chen Er'a's opium trafficking was real and sentenced Chen Er'a to one year of imprisonment for intending to sell and transport opium, with a fine of 300 yuan. If the fine was not paid after enforcement, two yuan would be converted to one day of imprisonment. The pretrial detention period would be deducted. The 105 taels of opium and the seven baskets of charcoal were confiscated. Chen Moji was acquitted and released.

Summary of the Rice Market Regulation Association Meeting 154

This summer, the price of rice in Shanghai continued to rise sharply during the transition between seasons. Although the price limit was 20 yuan per shi (unit of volume), the actual price exceeded this by 2 to 3 yuan. Residents found it difficult to obtain food, and with the urgent military situation in the front lines and instability in the rear, unscrupulous elements took the opportunity to incite unrest, posing a threat to the security of Shanghai. Yu Qiaqing, a leader in the business community, was deeply concerned about this and launched the Shanghai Rice Market Regulation Movement, preparing a large sum of one million yuan to purchase large quantities of rice in bulk and sell it at a loss to stabilize the rice price. The announcement of this plan immediately caused the rice price to fall. After the Rice Market Regulation Association held a meeting yesterday, a reporter from the Guowen News Agency, recognizing the significant impact of the association's actions on the rice market, visited the association's chairman, Yu Qiaqing, to inquire about the association's work. Mr. Yu stated that the Rice Market Regulation Movement could be considered a success, and the Ministry of Finance and the Municipal Government had provided strong support, each allocating 50,000 yuan in silver. The Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement allocated 100,000 yuan in silver and planned to continue providing support. Fortunately, there was a good harvest in various regions, and the price of rice gradually decreased, eliminating the need to lose all the planned funds. However, because the price decreased significantly, the loss per shi exceeded the initial estimate, which was a fortunate outcome, as residents could purchase cheaper rice. In conclusion, the success of this effort was partly due to the cooperation of the Shanghai Municipal Council, demonstrating the importance of Sino-foreign cooperation. Mr. Yu then showed the reporter the letters to be sent to the Ministry of Finance and the Municipal Government, which are transcribed below: (1) Regarding the Shanghai rice price, which continued to rise sharply before the establishment of the Association, it was difficult for the citizens to obtain food. In the autumn when the crops were not yet ready, the military situation in the front lines was tight, and the people in the rear were facing a food shortage. The problem of public order was precarious. Therefore, since the establishment of the Association, large quantities of rice have been purchased, and we have declared that we will sell at a loss to stabilize the rice price. As a result, those who hoard, speculate, monopolize, and manipulate the market dare not raise prices excessively and sell them at a reduced price. The rice price has continued to fall, by a total of four to five yuan. Fortunately, new grains have been harvested and there have been bumper crops in various places, the military situation has ended, public order is not a concern, and the price of rice has continued to decline. Although it cannot be said that the Association has completely suppressed the rice price, it has had some effect in regulating the rice market, which is something that we are able to inform your departments about. Here is a summary of the funds collected and the amount lost: We have received a total of 50,000 yuan in silver from your Ministry, 50,000 yuan in silver from the Municipal Government and the Ministry of Finance, and 100,000 yuan in silver from the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession. We have purchased three batches of foreign rice, each batch consisting of 15,000 bags, for a total of 45,000 bags, totaling 50,400 shi. The purchase price was 7 taels and 9 qian of silver per 100 jin. The first batch was calculated at 150 jin per shi, totaling 17 yuan and 2 jiao of silver. The second and third batches were calculated at 7 taels and 7.5 qian of silver per 100 jin, totaling 17 yuan of silver per shi. 26,804 shi and 9 dou and 6 sheng have already been sold, losing 2 yuan and 4 jiao and 5 fen, 4 yuan and 2 jiao, 2 yuan and 1 jiao, and 4 yuan respectively, totaling 82,467 yuan and 8 jiao and 4 fen. There are still 23,595 shi and 4 he that have been sold but not delivered. Because the price of rice has fallen sharply, they can only be sold for 10 yuan and 1 jiao of silver per shi, losing 6 yuan and 9 jiao of silver per shi, totaling 162,805 yuan and 7 jiao and 8 fen. The total loss is 245,273 yuan and 6 jiao and 2 fen. In addition, adding in the costs of weighing, warehousing, and other expenses, the total loss is approximately 256,000 yuan. We are now requesting that your Ministry allocate an additional 30,000 yuan in silver in addition to the 50,000 yuan previously allocated to help us close the operation. After the closing is completed, we will prepare a detailed list and report it to you. We would like to request that you investigate and promptly allocate the 30,000 yuan in silver to facilitate the closing.

Study and Improve the Manufacture of Mechanized Egg Yolks 158

The Commodity Inspection Bureau Sent a Letter to the Egg Factory Trade Association Calling for Attention to Research

The Shanghai Egg Factory Trade Association stated that the U.S. government had strictly revised its regulations since 1923, limiting the acidity of imported Chinese egg yolks to five degrees. Egg yolks exceeding this limit would be rejected as spoiled. However, from manufacturing to delivery to the United States, the egg yolks manufactured by various egg factories in our country often take more than six months. It is difficult to guarantee that the acidity will not gradually increase. If the acidity increases to five degrees when they arrive in the United States, they will not be allowed to be imported, and the impact will be significant. To prevent this problem, the association recently consulted with the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau to discuss relief measures. It is heard that the Inspection Bureau believes that if high-quality fresh eggs are used and manufactured according to scientific principles, egg yolks can be stored for a long time, even for two years, without spoiling under normal circumstances. The fact that the acidity of egg yolks manufactured by various egg factories in our country increases to five degrees after six months suggests that there are imperfections in the manufacturing materials and methods. Therefore, the Bureau sent a letter to the association urging them to improve the manufacturing using the most rigorous scientific methods so that the foreign trade of egg yolks would not be affected by the new U.S. regulations.

Funding Secured for Dredging Yu Tang River 159

The Yu Tang River in Shanghai County is an important river that has gradually become silted in recent years. Therefore, the County Construction Bureau and local figures have discussed plans for dredging. Funding for dredging the river has been requested by the County Government from the Provincial Financial and Construction Departments, which has been approved by the Provincial Finance Department and submitted to the Provincial Government. It has been determined that the Yu Tang River is an important river in the county and that dredging it is a key local water conservancy project. Therefore, it is approved that 1 jiao per mu be collected from the busy season land tax on the farmland benefiting from the river on both banks this year, and 5 fen per mu be collected from the upper busy season land tax in the twentieth year. The County Construction Bureau Director Wu has already submitted the budget for dredging expenses, standard cross-section drawings, a list of earthwork, a longitudinal profile of Yu Tang, and topographic maps to the Construction Department for review. It is also learned that the dredging expenses will be collected locally by the beneficiaries following the old precedents of the Qing Dynasty. Landowners will provide food, tenants will provide labor, and the amount of dredging will be determined based on the distance from the river and the amount of benefit received.

Bank of China Inspection Report 162

No. 32

The 32nd Inspection Report of the Shanghai Bank of China Issuance Reserve Inspection Committee: According to the rules of the committee, the committee members and appointed accountants inspected the issuance and interbank use of convertible note reserves of the Shanghai Bank of China Main Branch on October 26, 1930. The Director of the Monetary Department of the Ministry of Finance also participated in the inspection. The results of the inspection are listed below: The total amount of convertible notes issued is 122,133,372.85 yuan, of which the number issued by the Main Branch is 61,630,774.45 yuan, the number used by the Interbank is 28,020,774.40 yuan, and the number used by various banks is 32,481,824.00 yuan. Except for the portion used by various banks, which will be inspected separately according to the original method, this inspection focused on the portion used by the Interbank, as follows: The amount of convertible notes issued by the Main Branch and used by the Interbank is 89,651,548.85 yuan. The amount of convertible note reserves of the Main Branch and Interbank is 89,651,548.85 yuan, of which the cash reserve is 53,932,024.39 yuan and the security reserve is 35,719,524.46 yuan. The above two items show that the cash reserve accounts for 60% and the security reserve accounts for 40%. All were inspected and found to be accurate. In accordance with Article 5 of the rules, this formal report is hereby submitted. October 26, 1930, Xu Kan, Director of the Monetary Department of the Ministry of Finance, Wang Yansong, Pei ○, representatives of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Chen Zeqing, Sun Jingya, representatives of the Shanghai Banking Association, Wang Boxun, Hu Xisheng, representatives of the Shanghai Money Trade Association, Fan Zhengmei, Xi Qisun, representatives of various banks issuing notes, Li Zhilian, Chen Guangfu, Zhou Zongliang, Ye Zhuotang, Xu Jiqing, representatives of the directors and supervisors of the Bank of China, accountant Wang Zikang.

National Opium Seizures by Railway Bureaus in the 18th Year of the Republic of China 163

Statistics from the Investigation Department of the Chinese National Anti-Narcotics Association

The Chinese National Anti-Narcotics Association this year collected statistical materials on opium prohibition throughout the country. Since transportation agencies on both land and water often discover and seize travelers carrying opium, raw opium, and narcotics, various institutions such as post offices and railway bureaus nationwide also collect such data. Regarding post offices, the Association's Investigation Department has already published the opium-related seizures in various newspapers. It is now reported that the anti-narcotics materials from various railway bureaus nationwide have been compiled by Zhou Chucai, the Director of Statistical Investigations of the Association. From January 1, 1929, to December 31, 1929, a total of 203 offenders were apprehended, and 31,457.4 taels of opium were seized. The details are as follows: Jinghu and Huhangyong Railways: 56 offenders, 7,569 taels of opium; Jinpu Railway: 20 offenders, 2,223.9 taels; Jiaoji Railway: 6 offenders, 172.4 taels; Pinghan Railway: 23 offenders, 4,614.8 taels; Beining Railway: 17 offenders, 1,477 taels; Nanxun Railway: 3 offenders, 1,349 taels; Guangjiu Railway: 11 offenders, 901 taels; Yuehan Railway (Guangshao Section): 6 offenders, 227 taels; Yuehan Railway (Xiang'e Section): 14 offenders, 11,869 taels; Shenhai Railway: 2 offenders, 60 taels; Jichang Railway: 35 offenders, 52.5 taels; Jidun Railway: 3 offenders, 16.8 taels; Tao'ang Railway: 1 offender, 19 taels; Sitao Railway: 4 offenders, 408 taels; Huhai Railway: 2 offenders, 22 taels. Total: 203 offenders, 31,457.4 taels. The above statistics are from the fifteen railway administrations. The Longhai and Pingsui Railways have not yet submitted their reports due to transportation disruptions. It is also noted that no passengers were found to be carrying raw opium. The Yuehan Railway (Zhushao Section), Zhangsha Railway, and Qike Railway seized narcotics but no opium. The Xinning Railway, Jihai Railway, Daoqing Railway, and Zhengtai Railway seized neither opium nor narcotics. Additionally, the Cangshi and Taosuo Railways are not included as they have not yet been completed. The Association is also analyzing the narcotics seized by the various railway bureaus, such as morphine, red pills, and white pills, and will soon publish a joint report with the postal service seizures.

News from Trade Associations 165

Paint Industry: The Paint Industry Trade Association held a meeting of its executive committee yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM at its association hall located at No. 5 Guoyutang Street, Xuelongdi, inside the city. Du Gengsheng served as the temporary chairman. After formalities, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting. Subsequently, all executive committee members took their oaths of office. Representatives then delivered speeches. The meeting adjourned with the sound of a bell. At 4:00 PM, the meeting continued, and Du Gengsheng, Zhou Shanqing, Xu Shunrong, Xiao Peisheng, and Wang Shengcai were elected as standing committee members. Du Gengsheng was elected chairman from among the standing committee members. Ni Fusheng, Zhang Fukang, Yun Xiang, Pan Pinshan, Chen Yougeng, Xu Guoqing, Ling Youqiao, Shen Shuitang, Lian Wenbin, and Cai Lanzhou were elected as executive committee members. Ni Fusheng and Zhang Fukang were mutually elected as the Director and Deputy Director of the General Affairs Department, Xiao Peisheng and Xu Shunrong as the Director and Deputy Director of the Finance Department, Ling Youqiao and Ma Yunxiang as the Director and Deputy Director of the Investigation Department, Chen Yougeng and Xu Guoqing as the Director and Deputy Director of the Mediation Department, and Shen Shuitang and Pan Pinshan as members of the Valuation Committee. Ma Zhigang was hired as an assistant. Next, Secretary Xian Xingchu submitted various proposals for discussion: (1) The proposal to borrow and collect rent from the Finance Bureau was resolved to await a reply from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce before making a decision. However, as the association is newly established and its funding is insufficient, the maximum amount to be collected will be limited to one month's rent based on the assessed value on the housing tax bill. (2) The proposal for membership fees for the Chamber of Commerce was resolved to be determined after the capital amount of the fellow tradesmen is investigated and registered, and then submitted to the general assembly for approval. (3) The proposal to issue certificates and badges to members was resolved to be handled by the General Affairs and Finance Departments. (4) The proposal to collect membership fees was resolved to be implemented from November 1st. Other proposals, such as hiring a secretary and revising the fees for various guilds, will be submitted to the next executive committee meeting for approval. At this time, the bell rang for 7:00 PM, and the meeting was adjourned.

Cinder Factory Industry: The Cinder Factory Industry Trade Association held its inaugural meeting at the association hall the other day and elected executive committee members. Ma Shaoquan was elected as the temporary chairman. After formalities, the chairman delivered a report, followed by the election of executive committee members by the members present. Ma Shaoquan, Jin Hongfang, Wang Shaocheng, Xu Youren, Zhang Jingliang, Li Songtang, Xie Peixing, Lu Ganru, He Zhezhi, Li Renfu, and Lu Zigeng were elected as executive committee members. Most of the votes went to Hu Yaochuan, Zhang Yongtang and Hu Yun. The three took their oaths of office, and the meeting adjourned.

Weather Report 166

The Xujiahui Observatory's meteorological forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that it would be cold and cloudy, with strong northerly winds over the Yellow Sea and East China Sea. The weather in southern Japan is bad due to a low-pressure system moving northeast. There is a low-pressure system southeast of Okinawa in the Pacific Ocean. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the lowest temperature in this city was 70.3, and the highest was 58.1. On the same day last year, the highest temperature was 72.7, and the lowest was 55.9.
