Free Talk

A Word or Two 167

— Xin Mu

When a person's sorrow reaches its extreme, tears are exhausted, and only mad laughter remains.

If you find divorce too troublesome, you might as well add a clause to your marriage contract in advance: "Future separations are at each party's discretion."

The word "love" is attainable by everyone, but only temporarily by some, and permanently by few.

Don't envy others; know that others are envying you.

Those who truly understand freedom can enjoy it; those who cannot control themselves feel unfree everywhere.

Those who love others are loved; those who respect others are respected. Those who are arrogant and delight in attacking others' shortcomings will inevitably face others' contempt and criticism.

Although a mirror can reflect one's face, it cannot reflect the heart within.

The workers daily joyfully envy the boss's happiness and wealth, but they never know that his inner suffering is even greater than theirs.

The husband envies his wife's ease, while the wife says men are happy. In reality, it's six of one, half a dozen of the other. How many people in the world are truly at ease?

Those with a narrow mind cannot tolerate others and will never achieve great things.

Those who are despised everywhere blame the coldness of human feelings instead of recognizing their own faults. This is simply a blind heart.

What I Know of "Mr. Hui" 168

— Zhao Dingming

Mr. Hui, also named Guang, courtesy name Siwen, was from Qingjian County, northern Shaanxi, only ninety li from Wangyaobao, jointly governed by my Fushi and Anding, a day's walk away. There is a children’s rhyme: "Qingjian's stone slabs, Yaobao (i.e., the popular name for Wangyaobao) has coal, Suide has women, and Mizhi has men." The rocks of Qingjian are cyan, firm, and thin. With a little effort from stonemasons, they can be made into squares and circles of any size. Wangyaobao is located in the center of Anding, with connections in all directions. Coal mines are everywhere. The northern lands are extremely cold in winter. Having this natural fuel, one does not feel it. Therefore, the counties all envy it and have this song. As for the women of Suide, it is said to refer to Diaochan of the Three Kingdoms. The men of Mizhi refer to Lu Bu. In fact, Suide and Mizhi are prosperous and absorbed culture earlier than other counties. Men's and women's clothing is also more fashionable than in other counties.

When Mr. Hui returned to his hometown from abroad, it caused a sensation in northern Shaanxi. I was just a child at the time, entering school. The school's teaching methods were autocratic. All day long, the sound of reading aloud could not stop. Therefore, I did not know anything about Mr. Hui. In the fifth year of the Republic, the bandit Guo Jian disturbed northern Shaanxi, breaking Qingjian on the third day of the third month and Suide on the fifth day. My elder brother, Dingli, was studying at the Suide Elementary School and was killed. My family was greatly affected. In the sixth year of the Republic, the bandits Zhang Qingshan and Li Qinglan were incorporated in northern Shaanxi. Mr. Hui, seeing this, sold his property to engage in revolution and allied with Zhang and Li, greatly softening them. In the eighth month, Mr. Hui came to my fortress one day and rode with Zhang and Li in the suburbs. At that time, I still had two small braids hanging behind my head. One day after school, I saw his demeanor. He was less than five feet tall, with disheveled short hair, refined and cultured. The words "foreign student" were the catchphrase of my peers. A few days later, I heard that he had returned. Two days later, there was a burst of gunfire on the riverbank east of the city. I followed the sound to the top of the city, where the spectators were many. More than ten corpses lay in pools of blood below the city. They had secretly gone out at night to cause trouble and were discovered by Zhang and Li. They were executed by firing squad the next day. From then on, the people dared to interact with the soldiers without fear of being violated. It was Mr. Hui's initiative that made Zhang and Li's discipline so strict and meritorious. On August 26th of that year, Zhang and Li left northern Shaanxi from Wangyaobao via Mr. Hui to join the Jingguo Army and carry out the revolution. This is probably what is recorded in the reports about Mr. Hui, that "in the sixth year of the Republic, he raised five hundred men in northern Shaanxi, calling it Mr. Hui's army." After that, due to inconvenient transportation, everything was unknown. Only when Mr. Hui went to southern Shaanxi with Zhang and Li, for the sake of his family and hometown, he instructed Zhang and Li to pretend to be forced to leave Shaanxi when changing defenses from Yongping Town to Qingjian, in order to keep his family safe. Now, for more than ten years, the political situation has changed repeatedly, and the women and children of Guanzhong have all passed this on as a good story, and they respect his wisdom, courage, and contributions to the party and the country.

At 11:00 AM on October 26th, Mr. Yu Youren, a member of the Central Committee, and famous people from Shaanxi, including Sun Weidong, Yang Quanjun, Hu Jingquan, Zhou Yaowu, and Ma Wanyan, initiated a memorial service at the Yufo Zen Temple on Binlang Road in western Shanghai. Due to economic and time constraints, I was unable to attend, so I wrote this article to express my admiration.

Trivial Talks on Autumn Chrysanthemums 169

— Yang Yixiao

Chrysanthemum Wine: Brewed with chrysanthemum leaves, this wine can cure illness.

Chrysanthemum Cake: Remove the hearts of chrysanthemum petals, then mix them evenly with glutinous rice flour, rice flour, and white sugar. Steam in a cake steamer until cooked. It is fragrant, sweet, and delicious. Adding red and green threads makes it even more beautiful.

Chrysanthemum Mountain: Select various famous chrysanthemums and plant them in pots. Use red wood to frame them, arranging them in a high-low and varied manner to form a chrysanthemum mountain. It is elegant and pleasing to the eye.

Chrysanthemum Pool: Chrysanthemum Pool is located in Nanyang Prefecture, on the northwest bank of Neixiang. There is chamomile growing nearby. Drinking this water promotes longevity because the chrysanthemum is a longevity guest, so drinking chrysanthemum water also leads to longevity.

Chrysanthemum Pillow: Many used Hang Chrysanthemums, which have been soaked, are often discarded. If accumulated daily and placed in a bamboo basket and dried in a ventilated place, they can be used as a pillow. This is not only a utilization of waste, but can also clear heat and improve eyesight.

Motherly Love 170

— Miao Zi

Mr. Shaw said, "There is nothing in the world as cruel as war, and there is nothing as peaceful as a mother's love. A mother and her son or daughter are like being side by side in an equation. A mother fully gives her heart, strength, wisdom, experience, and property to her children, as if it is a mathematical "transposition" in this equation. When the number on the children's side reaches its highest degree, the quantity on the mother's side equals zero. But there is no mother in the world who is not willing to sacrifice herself to support her children." These words are truly wonderfully lovely and admirably cautionary.

However, the price that children pay in front of their mothers is often not commensurate. Filial sons and daughters are rare after all, but ungrateful offspring can often be read about in today's social news. I still remember watching the film "慈母"OvertbeHiiil three years ago and being deeply moved. Little lambs who have sweetly slept in the warm embrace of their mothers, ah, you should know how to passionately repay your mothers!

The most tragic thing is that mothers sacrifice themselves to cultivate their children, but the children grow up and abandon their mothers. This kind of thing also happens a lot. There is no need to look for any real evidence. Just look at Ningbo. There is a fairy tale that says that an old female beggar often scolded young people on the street. People all said that she was crazy. Later, someone who knew her history told people, "Her son is still a student studying abroad and is very successful now. That woman raised her son from a young age to adulthood, and it took a lot of effort. Who knew that after her son's feathers were full, he would forget his mother's nurturing grace, so she went crazy."

Also, recently, the Star Film Company has a film "A Prostitute's Virtuous Mother." The content is also about a mother who, in order to cultivate her daughter, endures the shame of working in a brothel to provide her daughter with tuition fees. Although she has suffered a lot of anger, she always wholeheartedly expects her daughter to succeed. Unexpectedly, her daughter grew up and found out that her mother was a prostitute and, without asking the reasons, thought it was a great humiliation to herself and left without saying goodbye. Her mother was extremely anxious when she found out and searched everywhere, eventually going crazy and almost losing her life. Later, she was rescued after attempting to drown herself in the river. The newspaper published the story, and her daughter finally saw it and realized her ingratitude and returned to visit her mother. However, the mother's illness was already beyond help. We try to look at how touching and profound the plot of this film is! I hope that all daughters who have mothers can learn some lessons from this film, just as all sons can learn some lessons from the "Loving Mother" film. Then, Star Company's "A Prostitute's Virtuous Mother" can be considered a success after all.

The Strange Image of the Osmanthus Banquet 171

— Zheng Yimei

In Wuzhong, many large buildings and courtyards are planted with parasol trees and osmanthus trees, taking their cool shade and refreshing cleanliness. In Fengxi, near the city, Zhu Zenan is a scholar who, after chanting, likes to plant flowers and cultivate bamboo, not begrudging the labor of watering and weeding. There is an osmanthus tree grafted with a pomegranate. This autumn, the flowers are lush and have changed to crimson. He sings the praises of five osmanthus branches, and his inspiration soars. He then wrote invitations, inviting his literary friends to the osmanthus flower party. For a time, the skirts and shoes of the guests came in droves, and the poetry and wine flowed freely. A certain gentleman in the seat and others carried a camera for photography, and thus took a photo of the osmanthus association chanting picture as a memento. The next day, the certain gentleman developed the image and was surprised. Next to the osmanthus tree there was a woman. Between indistinct impressions, her hair fine, her eyebrows beautiful. The owner, Zhu Zenan, was also surprised and did not know why. Because on the day of the party, the NIngxiang Hall and boudoir were separated and there were no family members present. He showed the developed image to the present literary friends and none could explain it. Some said that there were records of flower demon and tree spirits in historical anecdotes. This must be a flower demon and tree spirit. Some friends advised the host, Zhu Zenan to cut down the tree to prevent disaster, but Zhu Zenan was never superstitious. Thus, the tree still casts its shadow as before. I had the photograph passed on to me. I viewed it and the description was accurate. Being curious, I recorded the matter thus.

Nanyang Travelogue (68) 172

— Ling Hua

Eyebrows are raised and mountains are painted. Bobo Village has dozens of miles of land, the people are few, and the springs are beautiful. If Chinese people can manage orchards here, they will surely reap great profits. It is also possible to build roads and establish hospitals here. This place is in the middle of the north and south and is only one day from Yangon. Those who are suffering from heat-related illnesses can come here for treatment. If we govern this village, it will be no different from an Arcadia. The land can be bought and is not expensive. Burma is peaceful, and bandits are extremely rare. Thieves may or may not be concerned.

A friend said, "Siam and Burma are both Buddhist countries. There is no need to worry about the communist men. Their maleness is subdued by the Buddha, so their hearts are easy to govern. Subdue the male gender, and the world will be peaceful. There is no other secret technique."

Yin Jun's mother's fiftieth birthday was on the fourth. At dawn, the yellow-robed monks were full of seats. The mother, son, and the entire family knelt one by one, offering milk tea and listening to the lecture. Each monk held a bowl. I now had the opportunity to strike the bowl with my hand and test its quality. It had two layers. The lower layer was made of thin iron, and the upper layer was sand and mud with lacquer, which was very beautiful. There were also those made of tile and porcelain. The family placed a rice bowl in each bowl, with several small porcelain cups. Each cup contained chicken, fish, meat, etc. The large pieces of fatty meat were more than an inch thick. Seeing them, my chest felt nauseous. I could not agree with the Theravada teachings of Burma and Siam. Eating the flesh of living beings is no different from Confucianism. What ghostly words are there to say about universally saving people and heaven? It is too wasteful. It is fitting that the Burmese are poor and lazy, and monks are everywhere. Master Taixu's new monk system advocates that there should only be 500 monks per county in China, for a total of 1 million monks. If more knowledge is added, they can guide society. If there are too many, then it is unnecessary. But I advocate following the methods of the Chan school of ancestral work. Having many is also not a problem. If they sit and eat, then they should also be limited to 500 per county. The 500 are not just idlers. They have the Way and science to teach the youth. The effect will be higher than today's teachers who only know material science.

The Burmese treat monks as if they were Buddhas. When they arrive at home, they greet them and bow to them. The monks chant incessantly, and people also imitate them. If everyone in the world were like this, perhaps the evil flames of fierce bandits could also be restrained. However, in a well-off world, the country will surely perish. It is also difficult to say for sure. Siam also practices Theravada and is now independent and free, recovering extraterritorial rights, which is better than us. The problem also lies in impure politics and diplomacy and in the military.

I have seen strange customs here. Some people carry large leather bags to transport water, which is close to the Indian style.

European Travelogue (82) 173

— Liu Haisu

Diary of a Tour of Italy

(3) Ten Days in Rome (5)

—The Eternal City La ville eteinelle

June 1st—Exhibition of Spanish Masterpieces and Exhibition of Modern Japanese Painting

It was past twelve o'clock when we came out of the Spanish Exhibition. We wanted to find a cheap and good restaurant to have lunch, but in vain we circled several streets under the scorching sun and turned back and forth, and finally could not find a small restaurant. My feet were sore and I was extremely hungry, so I braced myself and walked into a magnificent Restaurant. Several waiters in ink-black礼服 with shiny hair led us from the door into the dining room and greeted us very diligently. I first drank a few mouthfuls of cold water, and the heat in my heart was reduced by half. Two waiters in equally grand attire each held a beautiful menu for us to look at. Everyone's eyes were ink-black and we could not recognize a single word. When we looked at each other, they almost laughed. This was not because it was ridiculous that we were illiterate, but because our expression was a bit ridiculous. Fortunately, they were accustomed to receiving foreigners, so they offered cold chicken, smoked beef, and the famous Italian pasta for you to choose from. I ordered frozen chicken and Italian pasta. It was extremely happy to eat these delicacies when hungry and thirsty. The scorching sun in Rome in June was truly terrifying. However, I was intoxicated in the beauty and ancient charm of Rome, and I was very excited. After lunch, my spirits were refreshed. We passed through the bustling street from the Piazza Venezia and a magnificent building stood before our eyes. This was the exhibition hall of the city of Rome, like the Grand Palais in Paris, dedicated to general exhibitions. The Japanese Art Exhibition was held inside. We walked in and took a quick tour. There were about twenty rooms, which the Japanese called the Imperial Palace style. The houses were decorated in an elegant and refined manner. Originally, their wood, wall panels, roofs, and even tatami mats were all transported from their country. The carvings on the screens and the potted flowers were purely Japanese in flavor. Speaking of their works, they are all from the hands of first-class modern masters in Japan. Among them, such as Yokoyama Taikan, Takeuchi Seiho, Shimomura Kanzan, Hirafuku Hyakusui, Kawai Gyokudo, Yamamoto Shunkyo, Kobori Tomoto, Hashimoto Kansetsu, Kaburaki Kiyokata, Araki Jippo, Komuro Suisho, Yuki Somei, Ishizaki Komyo, Nishimura Goun, and Domoto Insho, Yamauchi Tamon Tsutaya Ryukaku, the rest I can’t remember. Each person has fifteen or six works. Especially Yokoyama Taikan and Takeuchi Seiho are considered his door representatives. In the central and largest Royal Hall, there are extremely large Xiao Xiang Eight Views. They are considered innovators of Japanese painting. In my opinion, they are still imitating the style of Muqi, Ma Yuan, and Xia Gui.

Business News Finance

Fluctuations in the Gold Market 174

Long and short positions mutually control, resulting in hesitation. Yesterday's gold market was exceptionally confusing, with alternating advances and retreats. In the morning session, fluctuations of two or three taels were common, while the afternoon saw only one or two taels of movement, inevitably leading to uncertainty. Long and short positions were mutually controlling, although not as chaotic as the day before. Foreign exchange rates slightly softened, with banks engaging in mutual deposits and withdrawals. While trading among the various firms in the market was active, there were no large transactions. In the morning, Fuchang, Yifengyong, Hengxing, and Dadecheng, among others, were buying, while Yuanmaoyong, Yud, and Xinheng had already sold off. The morning market appeared sluggish, and there was no change in overseas gold markets, but exchange rates consistently declined. The hesitating state afterward stemmed from differing supply and demand. Prices had exceeded eighty-four taels, but the lowest point hovered just above eighty taels. The noon hour saw calm, but later, Chenggenghong, Fuxingyong, and arbitragers all entered the market. Yud, Wanxing, and Yongchengchang showed signs of selling. The initial opening was stable, but then became firmer, resulting in a situation similar to the previous day, with prices fluctuating like drifting duckweed.

US Silver Purchases Drive Down Gold Prices. The opening of the December market immediately fell by one tael, reaching 582 taels and 5 qian (gross margin within approximately three taels, once dropping to within two taels). Large bars did not change further. With news of slight purchases of silver bars in the US, market sentiment softened. Subsequently, Zifengyong, Taikangrun, and others bought in, which brought a recovery to 84 taels and 7 qian. Foreign exchange rates remained stable. Korea and Taiwan bought in the spot market. Dalian's silver was at a premium of 1 tael 2 qian 7 fen. Zhengjin traded March Sterling at 17375, then January at 375 could be settled, and Yuanmaoyong selling caused it to retreat to 3 taels 7 or 8 qian. When the initial posting was made, the listed price was around 4 taels. Except for the East Exchange, which was depressed by 0.25, there were no other changes, and it dropped to 3 taels 1 qian. Shortly after, it added 0.45 qian. However, Yuanmaoyong, Taikangrun, and arbitragers sold heavily, especially Sterling. Mitsui bought January, calculated at 174375, thus at 10:00, it fell to 80 taels 0 qian 6 fen. Guangbang Hengxing and others bought in and Zhengjin absorbed January Sterling at 17375. It has now returned to a high of over 2 taels. By 10:30, it rose to 83 taels 3 or 4 qian, but sellers remained strong, with Yud, Fuxingyong, Shunli, and Wanxing selling. Moreover, January Sterling could be settled at 17375, and Macalie and Korea sold it to Shengda and Dalianbang. The gold price then made a second downward move to 80 taels 0 qian 5 fen around 11:00. Afterward, it seemed to stabilize and rose about 2 taels. However, from 11:00 to 12:00, there were fluctuations of more than 1 tael. At closing, it was 82 taels 1 qian, a slight decrease of 0.3 or 0.4 qian. The posted price was changed to 623 taels 4 qian. The gold exchange opened lower by 0.25, initially pressing down to 40 taels, then between 43 and 41 taels.

Various Firms' Pursuits Create a Fluctuating Market. The afternoon market opened at 81 taels 9 qian (gross margin not initially disparate). Afterward, it rose from 81 taels 7 qian to 3 taels 8 qian as Zifengyong and Fuxingyong pursued. Then it slightly decreased by 0.7 or 0.8 qian. After 3:00, the buying side was active because HSBC was buying in, seeing Citibank at 39.125, and the January Sterling banking trade was at 17375. It thus rose to 84 taels 2 or 3 qian. Suddenly, Yud and Yongchengchang came to sell, and it immediately fell by more than 1 tael to 2 taels 7 or 8 qian at 3:30. At 4:00, Fuchang and Yuanheng bought in. Afterward, the market was mediocre, with only a few qian rising or falling. However, retail investors did not cease selling, which depressed it by slightly less than 1 tael to between 83 taels. At the 4:30 closing, it was 83 taels 4 qian, which was only 1 qian lower than the previous day, fluctuating again by 2 or 3 qian, totaling 3 taels 5 or 6 qian. The highest price during the day was 84 taels 7 qian, and the lowest price was 80 taels 5 qian, a difference of 4 taels 2 qian. Looking back at the posted prices, it was depressed by around 40 taels. Period Flour Turns Downward, Especially Near-Term 185

Yesterday, after the opening of the flour market in the morning and afternoon, the current month uniformly turned downward. The current month fell even more sharply due to warehouse receipt issues. Because the Chinese warehouse receipts from the previous month had not yet been cleared, the receiving side still returned them to the exchange. The customer groups had nowhere to go, and this street dared not receive a batch of bottom goods. No one inquired. Therefore, the standard market value had to be settled by many parties, and it opened lower and lower. It was finally heard that the factory itself was hedging and receiving it. The current month hedged out November, but the weakness was not reduced, and the lowest closing price fell to 2 taels 2 qian 4 fen 2 li and a half, nearly 0.5 fen lower than the previous day's highest price. The distant months also softened because the foreign wheat was also lower by 0.2 or 0.3 taels, and the recent period was also lower. Later, the market was even weaker due to the large factories issuing grades. As a result, the current month fell by 0.375 fen compared to the previous day, November fell by 0.125 fen, December fell by 0.1 fen, and February fell by 0.125 fen, and February fell by 0.15 fen.

Futures Wheat Market Fills Shorts and Recovers 186

Yesterday, the futures wheat market, after opening in the morning and afternoon, presented an initial fatigue followed by firmness. When it initially opened, the foreign wheat quotations turned lower, and market sentiment was naturally dampened, falling by 0.2 or 0.3 fen compared to the previous day's closing. Afterward, because the large short accounts intentionally filled the shorts for near and distant periods, their market sentiment was led by the flour seeing a rising image. However, in terms of the future, the flour price is so depressed that the opening price in the month is feared to re-enter a sluggish environment. If this is the case, there is nothing to do. As a result, November/December rebounded by 0.3 fen compared to the previous day, January rebounded by 0.3 fen, and February rebounded by 0.4 fen. The spot wheat market also saw higher prices because the recent arrivals were very quiet, and high-quality goods were even fewer. The existing stocks in the market could not help but become thinner, so medium-quality goods were also gradually driven up. Yesterday, various grades opened again, calling for 0.4 or 0.5 fen. Mingguang Xinchangzhou, Yaowan, and Xuzhou wheat, 1,650 bags, were purchased by Shen Da Xin Da and other factories.

Fluctuations in Overseas Silk Markets 187

In the past week, the Yokohama raw silk market saw prices gradually increase due to the frequent spot sales. The New York factories' telegraphic transfers also saw sharp increases of 30 to 40 taels. The foreign silk market had a hopeful turning point. However, yesterday afternoon, a Yokohama telegram suddenly reported a sharp drop of 30 to 40 yen in Japanese silk during the day, and the New York telegram also did not see a transfer. Overseas silk markets are fluctuating greatly. Both Chinese and foreign silk merchants are taking a wait-and-see approach, and the Shanghai market has also announced a halt.

Wuxi White Silk Factories Transport Large Quantities to Shanghai 188

The silk factories in Shanghai and Wuxi jointly went on strike the day before yesterday in protest against the public quantitative inspection agreement. It is estimated that eight out of ten silk factories in Shanghai are closed. Five out of ten factories in Wuxi are closed, and the rest are urgently in need of winding and unwinding silk due to their relations with the foreign houses' silk futures and the inability to store autumn cocoons (semi-baked cocoons) for a long time. They also plan to join the alliance. With the foreign houses' silk market increasingly sluggish, the foreign houses' silk futures have all been wound and unwound. It was decided to continue the closure from the first day of next month. Therefore, the white silk processed by various silk factories in Wuxi is being transported to Shanghai in batches. In recent days, the Beijing-Shanghai train has transported 570 pieces of white silk, preparing to be delivered to various foreign houses today. Yesterday, all the houses transported them to the Commodity Inspection Bureau for public quantitative inspection.

Shanghai Market

Market News 220

The newly opened Ronghua Socks Factory, located on the west side of the Hongkou Triangle Ground Vegetable Market, declares that the factory's double-shop Western-style storefront is richly decorated, promoting Chinese national products, purchasing global goods, and issuing Fortune Brand silk stockings, cotton stockings, and the factory's soaps, towels, cosmetics, velvet fabrics, and sanitary shirts and trousers. It will open on November 1st with a grand 30-day sale. The factory's goods are exquisite and the location is in a bustling downtown area, so a grand occasion is assured.

The Sanhe Company at 56 Nanjing Road declares that the company was the first to create and sell 3-4-5 ply table tennis boards and Japanese-style square and round boards. The styles are exquisite, the standards are reliable, and they are most suitable for competitions. They have long been praised by ladies and gentlemen from all walks of life. The prices are extremely low: 3 ply for 4 jiao, 4-5 ply for 5 jiao, and square/round for 6 jiao. Branch stores are located next to the Shanghai Grand Theater on North Sichuan Road, where they are also available for sale.

The Yongkang Electrical Appliance Factory in Jiugeng Lane, Hongkou, declares that the factory has been established for many years and produces excellent products. The Iron Anchor brand flashlights are sturdy and durable, with strong light and power saving. They are the best among flashlights and sales are particularly developed.

Moreover, Mr. Han's Painting 221

Guanshengyuan Food Company declares that the company has recently manufactured various candies, such as sandwich chocolate candies, cream chocolate candies, cream toffee, cherry blossom soft candies, orange blossom soft candies, and various Western-style imitation candies, with no fewer than hundreds of patterns. The decoration is artistically unique, and the flavors are especially fresh and delicious, and all are rich in nourishment. They are now being launched in large quantities. General buyers at the Nanjing Road main store of the Japanese company, as well as the Wangping Street West Branch and the Henan Road Old Nine Acres department stores, are quite satisfied.

The Sincere Company's Foreign Goods Department declares that hundreds of styles of pure wool sweaters have newly arrived in the city, with all sizes and colors available. The prices are particularly fair: men's are from 6 jiao 5 fen to 35 yuan per piece, women's are from 5 jiao to 8 yuan 5 jiao, and children's are from 2 jiao 5 fen to 3 yuan. In addition, there are many British pure wool sweaters with fashionable colors and soft textures, and various sports sweaters are also in stock. Recently, many athletes have come to select and purchase them daily. Furthermore, Sincere's own brand of Bai Lan Cream has a clear and elegant fragrance, moisturizes the skin, and enhances beauty. The price is low and it is now on the market, with sales everywhere brisk and greatly exceeding supply.

Theater News 222

Mingxing Film Company declares that the company has recently obtained an extremely good script with unique depictions of both comedy and tragedy. The entire plot is even more unusually tortuous and compact, and after additions and deletions by the company's major playwrights, it has become even more perfect. It has been named "Ling Fu Ling," and the roles are played by major stars such as Gao Qianping, Wang Mengshi, Gong Jianong, and Wang Zhengxin. As for the directing aspect, the original director Hu has devoted all his efforts to the production of the sound film "Singing Girl Red Peony," so it is co-directed by Tang Jie and Wang Jiting. The two gentlemen are well-versed in the art of screen performance, so there will surely be good results.

Inside the Alley 223

— Photo by Zhang Yian

The Daxin Ticket Office at 270 Huile Lane, Sanma Road, declares that since the ticket office began soliciting members, dozens of people have joined daily, and the membership is flourishing. It has newly hired Qingyi teacher Fang Yunbiao, Laosheng teacher Zhang Yunlong, Qin teachers Yang Zilin and Chen Jinkui, and Drum teacher Xu Ruiting. The membership fee is 2 yuan per month. Send a stamped addressed envelope for regulations.

The Central Grand Theater declares that the theater will begin showing "Eastern Two Knights" today. The film's production is quite meticulous, with clever mechanisms in the Buddhist temple. Any woman with beauty is bound to fall into a trap, but the evil-doing monks are eventually destroyed by the knights. The narration is as winding as a sheep's intestine, confusing and bewildering. It also expresses folk love and Robin Hood chivalry, and the scene of attacking the fortress at night, with horses galloping and torches blazing, is a magnificent spectacle.

Publishing News 224

Dr. Lu Jinhou, former president of Donglu University, Yunnan Education Director, and current professor of political science at Daxia University and Central University, has recently published "Travels in Fifteen European and American Countries," published in full in two volumes, with an additional volume of about 100,000 words. This is the author's diary of his travels to various advanced European and American countries while studying abroad, with interspersed narratives and discussions, uniquely ingenious. The first volume is "Travels in the New World," the second volume is "Travels in European Countries England, France, Switzerland, Belgium, Germany, Austria, Italy, Russia," and an additional volume includes "Travels in China Datong, Yanzi Rock, Jiaoshan," and "Educational Survey of the Nine Provinces of Jiangsu and Jin." There is also a long preface in which the author describes his impressions of Japan, the New World, Europe, and various provinces in China after traveling around the world. The greatest feature of this book is that the author explores and criticizes the cultures, systems, and customs of various European and American countries with a purely objective attitude. The narrative is concise, the investigation is accurate, the writing is magnificent, and the vision is far-reaching, making it a rare and excellent book in the genre of travel writing. The price is one yuan. Sales locations: Shanghai Daxia University, Xinyue Bookstore, Nanjing Central University.

Page 23

Book Review

The Tibet Question 225

— Tang Bin

Edited by Hua Qiyun

At a time when the great powers are staring covetously at China and actively plotting against our border defenses, any pioneering work concerning Mongolia and Tibet is bound to deeply affect the livelihood of the people of the whole country. It is most distressing that our compatriots lack the courage and organization to make a great determination to investigate or develop these regions. However, the British pay great attention to Tibet, and the Japanese and Russians pay great attention to Mongolia. Their knowledge of these two places is more practical and abundant than ours. Sometimes we even have to use their books as research and reference materials. How shameful is this! Mr. Hua's book calls for a fundamental solution to all important matters concerning our border defenses, which is why such great achievements are presented before our eyes.

The entire book is divided into three parts. The first part is "The Geography of Tibet." The first chapter, "General Discussion of Tibet," focuses on the development of Tibet itself, and is further divided into four sections: (1) The name and situation of Tibet, (2) The area and population of Tibet, (3) The divisions of Tibet, and (4) The important cities of each division. The second chapter, "The Topography of Tibet," describes Tibet's geology, terrain, mountains, rivers, climate, and rainfall. The third chapter, "The Economic Situation of Tibet," describes Tibet's products, industry, commerce, and transportation. The fourth chapter, "The Social Conditions of Tibet," describes the distribution of Tibet's people, their way of life, customs, and etiquette, the relationship between written language and spoken language, as well as education and religion, etc. The fifth chapter, "A Glimpse of the Journey to Tibet," includes more than fifty stations, each with detailed explanations. The sixth chapter, "The Border Defenses of Tibet," describes the important passes of Tibet, the small countries along the border, Pianma, and the Savage Mountain, etc. After reading this part, one can understand the general outline of the entire Tibet, as well as the content of its topography and culture. If we need to acquire all knowledge about Tibet and the location of Tibet's border defenses, we should read this part carefully, so that it can prepare us with many plans for "going to Tibet."

The second part is "The Politics of Tibet," and like the previous part, it is divided into six chapters. The first chapter, "The Relationship between the Tang, Song, Yuan, and Ming Dynasties and Tibet," is divided into six sections: (1) The origins of the Tibetan people, (2) The relationship between the Tang Dynasty and Tibet, (3) The relationship between the Song Dynasty and Tibet, (4) The relationship between the Yuan Dynasty and Tibet, (5) The relationship between the Ming Dynasty and Tibet. The second chapter, "The Pacification of Tibet in the Early Qing Dynasty," describes the beginning of the Qing court's communication with Tibet and the Qing court's pacification of Tibet. The third chapter, "The Qing Court's Management of Tibet during the Flourishing Qing Dynasty," describes the origins of the Qing court's management of Tibet and its achievements. The fourth chapter, "The Qing Dynasty's Management of Kangzang in the Late Qing Dynasty," describes the evolution of the boundaries of Xikang, the process of becoming an internal dependency, the content of the county administration, and the advance of troops into Tibet and the Dalai Lama's exile, etc. The fifth chapter, "The Rampancy of Tibetan Bandits against Us since the Republic of China," describes the first internal invasion by Tibetan bandits after the establishment of the Republic of China, the second internal invasion in 1917, and the recent large-scale internal invasion. The sixth chapter, "The Current Situation of Kangzang and the Necessity of Establishing a Province," describes the current situation of Xikang, the current situation of Tibet, and the necessity of establishing a province in Kangzang. After reading this part, one can certainly understand the origins of the Tibetan people and prove the long history of assimilation between China and Tibet. One can also see the historical evolution of the relationship between China and Tibet from the relationship between our country and Tibet throughout the dynasties. Finally, the author explains the necessity of changing it into a province so that imperialism cannot continue to covet it secretly. Of course, this part is as important as the previous one.

The third part is "The Diplomacy of Tibet," which is also divided into six chapters. The first chapter, "Tibet under the Encirclement of the Great Powers," is divided into four sections: (1) The Exploration of Tibet by the Great Powers, (2) The Coveting of Tibet by Britain and Russia, (3) The Conflict between Britain and Russia in Tibet, and (4) The Accommodation between Britain and Russia in Tibet. In this chapter, the author exposes the conspiracies of the two countries, allowing us to thoroughly understand the intentions of red and white imperialism. The second chapter, "The British Vanguard for the Invasion of Tibet," describes the process of the British annexation of Sikkim, the relationship between Britain and Bhutan, Nepal, and the detachment of Myanmar, etc. The third chapter, "The Beginning and End of the Sino-Tibetan-British Negotiations," describes the first armed conflict between Tibet and Britain and the conclusion of the Tibetan-Indian Treaty, the process of concluding the Tibetan-Indian Supplementary Treaty, and the establishment of the Tibetan-Indian Trade Regulations, etc. The fourth chapter, "The Beginning of British Interference in Tibet," describes the beginning and end of the first and second British interferences in China's advance into Tibet. The fifth chapter, "The Simla Conference," describes the proposed disputes over the boundaries in the Simla Conference, the boundary issues after the breakdown of the conference, followed by the boundary issues after the internal invasion by Tibetan bandits and the opinions of all parties on the boundary issues, etc. The sixth chapter, "Recent Negotiations on Tibetan Cases," describes the Tibetan case after Aston's mission to China, the Tibetan case during the Washington Conference and the British Labor Cabinet. At the same time, it talks about the points that Chinese people should pay attention to regarding Tibet thereafter. The author has elaborated on the author's detailed account of the adventures of various countries in Tibet, so that Chinese people know the urgency of their encirclement of Tibet. As for the failure of negotiations with Britain over the years, it is used to clarify Britain's active attempts to plot Tibet and the need for the Chinese people to pay attention to Tibet in order to show the importance of building the border. This point is right at a time when the National Government is striving for construction, and our people can no longer ignore it.

Everyone knows that to save China from poverty, one must resolutely go to the important border defenses. Then Tibet is of course a place worthy of attention, and our determination to go there is not to seek fame and profit, but to embrace the spirit of personal sacrifice and seek permanent happiness for Mongolia, Tibet, and the entire China. Undoubtedly, this relies on the perseverance of enthusiastic people. Under the strong encirclement, we can no longer hesitate. However, the lack of knowledge of Mongolia and Tibet among Chinese people is also an intolerable fact. If we want to know everything about it first, then Mr. Hua's book is really worth recommending, and sincerely hope that readers will pay attention to this issue and regard "going to Mongolia and Tibet" for investigation as the goal.

Silver Shadow 226

— Wen Hua

By Wang Jiayu

This book is a collection of short stories, divided into eight parts: "Spirochete," "Autumn Rain," "I Can No Longer Love You," "Weariness," "Rainy Night," "Silver Shadow," "Father," and "Baby." Except for the last one, "Baby," they are all lively and powerful love stories.

"Spirochete" is the most brilliant one, breaking through the carnal atmosphere of the fin de siècle and imposing severe punishment. The protagonist, Han Qing, a young man who already has a pure lover, studies in Japan. He is purely and simply a victim who can represent being misled into lust and unable to extricate himself. When he was about to return home from Japan, under some kind of excitement and impulse, he fell in love with a Japanese servant girl and spent two carnal nights with her to his heart's content. Little did he know that after this indulgence, he had already contracted the so-called spirochete. He did not think about it, nor did he care about the pure lover who sincerely loved him, and only knew how to enjoy the pleasure of committing crimes for a while. However, this deeply embedded germ finally accompanied him back home. After returning, he and his pure lover

Page 24

Spent half a month of rosy life. Right after the engagement, the syphilis that he had never expected broke out, and then he deeply regretted it, and his conscience was almost driving him crazy. But on the one hand, he had to hide it from his lover and her mother and go to the hospital for treatment. After his lover knew the source of his illness, not only did she not blame or despise him, but she also comforted him very gently. But he could not bear this humiliation and finally committed suicide the next day. This is the author's punishment for him.

Let's see what the author borrows from Han Qing's mouth: "The Pingmei (that is, his lover) of today is not mine anymore. I am not qualified to love her anymore..."

"I am more despicable than anything else. I am more dirty than anything else. Beauty and happiness in life have nothing to do with me. What is the point of living..."

The author is truly a writer of conscience. How fiercely he despises the criminal protagonist, and how much he respects the sacred god of love. So he buried Han Qing mercilessly.

Here, the author exposes the so-called romantic youths of the fin de siècle who put "sacred love" in front of them as a protective charm, but in fact they are just mixing in a morbid sexual desire. Even more, some bored literati, using a romantic or even decadent tone, write some moanings without illness, monotonous and boring rubbish, harming a group of blind youths. This is truly sad! When the national spirit is declining to this point, we need our youths to turn weakness into strength. Can we sit back and watch the spread of this evil force? The author of this book has already helped us to rescue this crisis.

In the second chapter, "Autumn Rain," I feel that it is too rich in individual hedonism. There is a passage spoken from the mouth of the heroine Zhi Xin that can be used as proof of my observation:

"Ah—what a poetic realm this is. If we two could build three thatched cottages here and live out our lives, I would have no other requests."

This kind of selfish, individualistic idea is just the extravagant hope of people who are immersed in a rosy dream, or of people who are tired of the world and only seek to live out their short lives comfortably. It is the so-called garden of Edenism of our Mr. Tao Qian. However, at least our youths should not have this idea. The burden of the future should belong to our youths. Of course, some people think that love is sacred and supreme, and that everything can be sacrificed for love, as long as love can be fulfilled. But I think that love is not necessarily so sacred and supreme. We only recognize that love is an important part of human life, and we must never use this to determine the entire meaning of life. So we must not prevent love, but we cannot "have no other requests." Perhaps this point was inadvertently slipped from the pen by the author. It was not necessary to nag so much, but I sincerely hope that the author can lead the youths who are trapped in confusion to this bright path.

"I Can No Longer Love You" can be said to be the longest chapter in the book. It mainly describes a literary writer, Li Danru, who once lost his love and developed a disgust for love, and formulated the philosophy of love that "the gift of love is tragedy." But later, under emotional impulse, he once again embarked on the path of love. He fell in love with a woman named Anna. When the two were swimming in the sweet sea of love, a completely romantic Miss Meimei came out. She also passionately pursued Li Danru. As a result, a triangular struggle was formed. But Danru did not love Miss Meimei at all, and even hated her for messing up the relationship between him and Anna. Miss Meimei used all kinds of divisive tactics, but Danru's repeated rejections were useless. Miss Meimei still stubbornly pursued him. Anna became jealous and misunderstood, and then became angry at Danru. So he still took back his previous philosophy of love and cruelly declared to Anna, "I can no longer love you."

This work can be said to be successful in terms of description, but it lacks a central consciousness and is slightly inferior to the first chapter, "Spirochete."

From the short piece "Weariness," we can be told the psychology of a person who is tossed up and down in the waves of love. The author once again used his means of exposure. It turned out that their love was so monotonous, and the highest point of their love was only expressed by kissing and hugging. So the author shouted "boring" for them. The author was able to write such vivid things in such short words, which cannot be regarded as exquisite.

"Two Nights" writes about the lonely psychology of a married woman, because soon after the marriage, her husband separated from her. So she was depressed and sought a place to vent her depression. This led her to pursue her uncle. The uncle is a very lovable young man. She used all means to express herself in front of him, but under the control of his mother, it was impossible. This piece is written very tensely and touchingly.

The content of "Father" seems to be a bit too coincidental. It tells the story of a illegitimate daughter who was abandoned by her father because he belonged to someone else less than four months after her birth. When she was six years old, her mother died. At the age of sixteen, she worked as an actress. Later, her father was able to recognize her in the section of recognizing relatives, using a red mole on the back of her mother's neck as an example. This is an old trick in coincidental stories and does not seem very beautiful.

"Silver Shadow" and "Baby" are also still good.

In summary, this book is a powerful work that can capture the psychology of the characters. However, there is one point that I hope the author will pay attention to: the self-admiration of the loners in the ivory tower is no longer needed in this era. I hope that the author will make further efforts for the nation in the future. This is my sincere hope.
